Editorial consensus was reached over the current list, so please do not remove any without discussing in the talk page.-->{{flatlist|\n* Singer-songwriter\n* producer\n* director\n* actress\n* businesswoman\n}}<!---occupation(s) artist is notable for, \"as given in the lead\", per: [[Template:Infobox person#Parameters]]-->\n| other_names        = Nils Sj\u00f6berg\n| years_active       = 2004\u2013present\n| awards             = [[List of awards and nominations received by Taylor Swift|Full list]]\n| website            = {{URL|taylorswift.com}}\n| module             = {{Infobox musical artist|embed=yes\n| origin             = [[Nashville, Tennessee]], U.S.\n| genre              = {{flatlist|\n* Pop\n* [[Country music|country]]\n* [[Folk music|folk]]\n* rock\n* [[alternative rock|alternative]]\n<!-- see the \"Musical Style\" section for references-->\n}}\n| instrument         = {{flatlist|\n* Vocals\n* guitar\n* banjo\n* piano\n* ukulele\n}}\n| label              = {{flatlist|\n* [[Republic Records|Republic]]\n* [[Big Machine Records|Big Machine]]\n<!--UMG is Swift's \"worldwide recorded music partner\"; Republic Records is her label in the US only according to a UMG press release (https://www.universalmusic.com/taylor-swift-signs-exclusive-global-recording-agreement-universal-music-group/)-->\n}}\n}}\n| signature          = File:Taylor Swift signature.svg\n}}\n'''Taylor Alison Swift''' (born December 13, 1989) is an American singer-songwriter.\u00a0Her discography spans multiple genres, and her narrative [[List of songs by Taylor Swift|songwriting]]\u2014often inspired by her personal life\u2014has received critical praise and media coverage. Born in [[West Reading, Pennsylvania]], Swift moved to [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]] at age 14 to become a [[Country music|country]] artist. She signed a songwriting deal with [[Sony Music Publishing|Sony/ATV Music Publishing]] in 2004 and a recording contract with [[Big Machine Records]] in 2005. Her 2006 [[Taylor Swift (album)|self-titled debut album]] made her the first female country singer to write or co-write a U.S. [[RIAA certification|platinum-certified]] album entirely.\n\nSwift's next albums, ''[[Fearless (Taylor Swift album)|Fearless]]'' (2008) and ''[[Speak Now]]'' (2010), explored [[country pop]]. The former's \"[[Love Story (Taylor Swift song)|Love Story]]\" and \"[[You Belong with Me]]\" were the first country songs to top the U.S. [[Mainstream Top 40|pop]] and [[Radio Songs (chart)|all-genre airplay]] charts, respectively. She experimented with rock and [[Electronic music|electronic]] styles on ''[[Red (Taylor Swift album)|Red]]'' (2012), which featured her first [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]] number-one song, \"[[We Are Never Ever Getting Back Together]]\", and eschewed her country image in her [[synth-pop]] album, ''[[1989 (Taylor Swift album)|1989]]'' (2014), supported by chart-topping songs \"[[Shake It Off]]\", \"[[Blank Space]]\", and \"[[Bad Blood (Taylor Swift song)|Bad Blood]]\". Media scrutiny inspired the [[Urban music|urban]]-flavored [[Reputation (album)|''Reputation'']] (2017) and its number-one single \"[[Look What You Made Me Do]]\".\n\nExiting Big Machine, Swift signed with [[Republic Records]] in 2018 and released her seventh studio album, ''[[Lover (album)|Lover]]'' (2019), followed by the autobiographical documentary ''[[Miss Americana]]'' (2020). She ventured into [[indie folk]] and [[alternative rock]] in her 2020 albums ''[[Folklore (Taylor Swift album)|Folklore]]'' and ''[[Evermore (Taylor Swift album)|Evermore]]'', whose singles \"[[Cardigan (song)|Cardigan]]\" and \"[[Willow (song)|Willow]]\" topped the Hot 100. Swift began [[Re-recording (music)|re-recording]] her first six albums after a [[Taylor Swift masters controversy|dispute]] over their [[Mastering (audio)|masters]], re-releasing two in 2021\u2014''[[Fearless (Taylor's Version)]]'' and ''[[Red (Taylor's Version)]]''. The latter's \"[[All Too Well (10 Minute Version)]]\" became the longest song to top the Hot 100. Her tenth album ''[[Midnights]]'' (2022) and its lead single \"[[Anti-Hero (song)|Anti-Hero]]\" broke numerous streaming records. Swift has self-directed music videos and films, such as ''[[All Too Well: The Short Film]]'' (2021), and had supporting roles in [[Taylor Swift videography|others]].\n\nHaving sold over 200 million records globally, Swift is one of the [[List of best-selling music artists|best-selling musicians of all time]]. She is the only act to have five albums open with over [[Lists of fastest-selling albums|one million copies sold]] in the US. Among [[List of awards and nominations received by Taylor Swift|her accolades]] are 11 [[Grammy Awards]], including three [[Grammy Award for Album of the Year|Album of the Year]] wins; an [[Emmy Awards|Emmy Award]]; 40 [[American Music Awards]]; 29 [[Billboard Music Awards|''Billboard'' Music Awards]]; and 84 [[Guinness World Records|''Guinness World Records'']]. Swift has been featured in rankings such as [[Rolling Stone's 100 Greatest Songwriters of All Time|''Rolling Stone''<nowiki/>'s 100 Greatest Songwriters of All Time]], [[Billboard (magazine)|''Billboard'']]'s Greatest of All Time Artists, the [[Time 100|''Time'' 100]] and [[Forbes Celebrity 100|''Forbes'' Celebrity 100]]. Honored with titles such as [[American Music Awards#Artist of the Decade|Artist of the Decade]] and [[Billboard Women in Music#Woman of the Decade Award|Woman of the Decade]], Swift is an advocate for artists' rights and [[women's empowerment]]. Her music is credited with influencing a generation of singer-songwriters.\n\n== Life and career ==\n=== 1989\u20132003: Early life and education ===\n[[File:Grandview Blvd 76, Wyomissing PA.JPG|thumb|Swift's childhood home in [[Wyomissing, Pennsylvania]]]]\nTaylor Alison Swift was born on December 13, 1989,<ref name=\":5\">{{Cite news|date=March 2, 2020 |title=Taylor Swift: The record-breaking artist in numbers|work=[[CBBC Newsround|Newsround]] |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/newsround/51711128|url-status=live|access-date=April 20, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200308182512/https://www.bbc.co.uk/newsround/51711128|archive-date=March 8, 2020}}</ref> at the [[Reading Hospital]] in [[West Reading, Pennsylvania]].<ref>{{Cite news|last=Sutherland|first=Mark|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/music/rockandpopfeatures/11430433/Taylor-Swift-interview-A-relationship-No-ones-going-to-sign-up-for-this.html |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/20220110/https://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/music/rockandpopfeatures/11430433/Taylor-Swift-interview-A-relationship-No-ones-going-to-sign-up-for-this.html |archive-date=January 10, 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live|title=Taylor Swift interview: 'A relationship? was rejected, however, because \"everyone in that town wanted to do what I wanted to do. So, I kept thinking to myself, I need to figure out a way to be different.\"<ref name=\"americansongwriter2\">{{Cite news|last=Malec|first=Jim|url=https://www.americansongwriter.com/2011/05/taylor-swift-the-garden-in-the-machine/|title=Taylor Swift: The Garden In The Machine|work=[[American Songwriter]]|date=May 2, 2011|access-date=May 21, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120510173906/http://www.americansongwriter.com/2011/05/taylor-swift-the-garden-in-the-machine/|archive-date=May 10, 2012}}</ref>\n\nWhen Swift was around 12 years old, computer repairman and local musician Ronnie Cremer taught her to play guitar. He helped with her first efforts as a songwriter, leading her to write \"Lucky You\".<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Martino|first1=Andy|title=EXCLUSIVE: The real story of Taylor Swift's guitar 'legend'|url=http://www.nydailynews.com/entertainment/music/computer-tech-taught-taylor-swift-guitar-exclusive-article-1.2072638|access-date=August 28, 2017|work=[[New York Daily News|Daily News]]|location=New York |date=January 10, 2015|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151122040522/http://www.nydailynews.com/entertainment/music/computer-tech-taught-taylor-swift-guitar-exclusive-article-1.2072638|archive-date=November 22, 2015}}</ref> In 2003, Swift and her parents started working with New York-based talent manager Dan Dymtrow. With his help, Swift modeled for [[Abercrombie & Fitch]] as part of their \"Rising Stars\" campaign, had an original song included on a [[Maybelline]] compilation CD, and attended meetings with major record labels.<ref name=\"americanbar\">{{cite web|title=americanbar.org PDF|url=http://www.americanbar.org/content/dam/aba/migrated/Forums/entsports/PublicDocuments/oppositionbrief.authcheckdam.PDF|access-date=April 18, 2012|publisher=Americanbar.org|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121011190303/http://www.americanbar.org/content/dam/aba/migrated/Forums/entsports/PublicDocuments/oppositionbrief.authcheckdam.PDF|archive-date=October 11, 2012}}</ref> After performing original songs at an [[RCA Records]] showcase, Swift, then 13 years old, was given an artist development deal and began making frequent trips to Nashville with her mother.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nbcnews.com/id/31032270/ns/dateline_nbc-newsmakers/t/tour-taylor-swift/|title=On tour with Taylor Swift \u2013 Dateline NBC|publisher=[[NBC News]]|date=May 31, 2009|access-date=July 1, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131005101242/http://www.nbcnews.com/id/31032270/ns/dateline_nbc-newsmakers/t/tour-taylor-swift/|archive-date=October 5, 2013}}</ref><ref name=\"Monsueto Ventures\">{{Cite magazine|last1=Castro|first1=Vicky|title=How to Succeed as an Entrepreneur, Taylor Swift Style|url=http://www.inc.com/vicky-castro/how-to-succeed-as-an-entrepreneur-taylor-swift-style.html|magazine=[[Inc. Swift|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=March 5, 2009|access-date=July 28, 2019|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190503043637/https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/the-very-pink-very-perfect-life-of-taylor-swift-107451/|archive-date=May 3, 2019}}</ref>\n\n=== 2004\u20132008: Career beginnings and first album ===\nIn Nashville, Swift worked with experienced [[Music Row]] songwriters such as [[Troy Verges]], [[Brett Beavers]], [[Brett James]], [[Mac McAnally]], and [[the Warren Brothers]]<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.americansongwriter.com/2011/05/taylor-swift-the-garden-in-the-machine/3/|title=Taylor Swift: The Garden In The Machine|work=[[American Songwriter]]|date=May 2, 2011|access-date=May 21, 2012|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130807054922/http://www.americansongwriter.com/2011/05/taylor-swift-the-garden-in-the-machine/3/|archive-date=August 7, 2013}}</ref><ref name=\"sonydeal\">{{cite web|url=http://www.bmi.com/news/entry/234444|title=Songwriter Taylor Swift Signs Publishing Deal With Sony/ATV|publisher=[[Broadcast Music, Inc.]]|date=May 12, 2005|access-date=April 20, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121204104706/http://www.bmi.com/news/entry/234444|archive-date=December 4, 2012}}</ref> and formed a lasting working relationship with [[Liz Rose]].<ref name=\"americansongwriter1\">{{cite web|last=Kosser|first=Michael|url=http://www.americansongwriter.com/2010/06/liz-rose-co-writer-to-the-stars/|title=Liz Rose: Co-Writer to the Stars|work=[[American Songwriter]]|date=June 3, 2010|access-date=April 19, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20111224215950/http://www.americansongwriter.com/2010/06/liz-rose-co-writer-to-the-stars/|archive-date=December 24, 2011}}</ref> They began meeting for two-hour writing sessions every Tuesday afternoon after school.<ref name=\"majorlyindie1\">{{Cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/features/liz-rose-songs-taylor-swift-little-big-town-20141024|title=Songwriter Spotlight: Liz Rose|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=October 24, 2014|access-date=September 24, 2016|last=Leahey|first=Andrew|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160926051735/http://www.rollingstone.com/music/features/liz-rose-songs-taylor-swift-little-big-town-20141024|archive-date=September 26, 2016}}</ref> Rose thought the sessions were \"some of the easiest I've ever done. Basically, I was just her editor. She'd write about what happened in school that day. She had such a clear vision of what she was trying to say. And she'd come in with the most incredible hooks.\" Swift became the youngest artist signed by the [[Sony/ATV Music Publishing|Sony/ATV Tree publishing house]],<ref>{{cite web|last=DeLuca|first=Dan|title=Focused on 'great songs' Taylor Swift isn't thinking about 'the next level' or Joe Jon as gossip|url=http://articles.philly.com/2008-11-11/news/25256467_1_big-machine-records-joe-jonas-country-music-association-awards|page=1|work=Philadelphia Daily News|access-date=April 17, 2012|date=November 11, 2008|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121118235847/http://articles.philly.com/2008-11-11/news/25256467_1_big-machine-records-joe-jonas-country-music-association-awards|archive-date=November 18, 2012}}</ref> but left the Sony-owned RCA Records at the age of 14 due to the label's lack of care and them \"cut[ting] other people's stuff\". She was also concerned that development deals may shelve artists,<ref name=\":29\" /><ref name=\"albuminfo\" /> and recalled: \"I genuinely felt that I was running out of time. I wanted to capture these years of my life on an album while they still represented what I was going through.\"<ref name=\":0\">{{Cite news|last=Preston|first=John|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/music/rockandpopmusic/5202294/Taylor-Swift-the-19-year-old-country-music-star-conquering-America-and-now-Britain.html|title=Taylor Swift: the 19-year-old country music star conquering America \u2013 and now Britain|work=[[The Daily Telegraph]]|access-date=August 30, 2012|date=April 26, 2009|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120105153224/http://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/music/rockandpopmusic/5202294/Taylor-Swift-the-19-year-old-country-music-star-conquering-America-and-now-Britain.html|archive-date=January 5, 2012}}</ref>\n\n[[File:Swift, Taylor (2007).jpg|alt=Taylor Swift singing on a microphone and playing a guitar|thumb|left|upright=1.2|Swift opening for [[Brad Paisley]] in 2007. To promote her [[Taylor Swift (album)|first album]], she opened tours for other country musicians in 2007 and 2008.<ref name=\"vh1country\">{{cite web|last=Rosa|first=Christopher|url=http://www.vh1.com/news/5861/opening-acts-bigger-than-headliner/|title=Opening Acts Who Became Bigger Than The Headliner|publisher=[[VH1]]|date=March 24, 2015|access-date=November 11, 2015|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151110191727/http://www.vh1.com/news/5861/opening-acts-bigger-than-headliner/|archive-date=November 10, 2015}}</ref>]]\nAt an industry showcase at Nashville's [[Bluebird Cafe]] in 2005, Swift caught the attention of [[Scott Borchetta]], a [[DreamWorks Records]] executive who was preparing to form an independent record label, [[Big Machine Records]]. She had first met Borchetta in 2004.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last1=Rapkin, Mickey |url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/7880979/the-bluebird-cafe-taylor-swift-dierks-bentley-oral-history|title=Oral History of Nashville's Bluebird Cafe: Taylor Swift, Maren Morris, Dierks Bentley & More on the Legendary Venue|magazine=Billboard|date=July 27, 2017|access-date=July 28, 2017 |url-status=live|archive-date=July 29, 2017 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170729142603/http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/7880979/the-bluebird-cafe-taylor-swift-dierks-bentley-oral-history}}</ref> She was one of Big Machine's first signings,<ref name=\":29\" /> and her father purchased a three-percent stake in the company for an estimated $120,000.<ref name=\"Taylor in Wonderland\">{{Cite magazine|last1=Hiatt|first1=Brian |date=October 25, 2012|title=Taylor Swift in Wonderland|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]] |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/news/taylor-swift-in-wonderland-20121025|url-status=live|access-date=August 1, 2016|archive-date=July 31, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160731171417/http://www.rollingstone.com/music/news/taylor-swift-in-wonderland-20121025}}</ref><ref name=\":30\">{{Cite news|last1=Greenburg|first1=Zack O'Malley|date=June 26, 2013|title=Toby Keith, Cowboy Capitalist: Country's $500 Million Man|work=Forbes |url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/zackomalleygreenburg/2013/06/26/toby-keith-cowboy-capitalist-countrys-500-million-man/2/|url-status=live|access-date=August 1, 2016|archive-date=August 27, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160827173032/http://www.forbes.com/sites/zackomalleygreenburg/2013/06/26/toby-keith-cowboy-capitalist-countrys-500-million-man/2/}}</ref> She began working on her [[Taylor Swift (album)|eponymous debut album]] with producer [[Nathan Chapman (record producer)|Nathan Chapman]], with whom she felt she had the right \"chemistry\".<ref name=\"albuminfo\" /> Swift wrote three of the album's songs alone, and co-wrote the remaining eight with Rose, [[Robert Ellis Orrall]], Brian Maher, and [[Angelo Petraglia]].<ref name=\"liner\">{{Cite AV media notes|title=Taylor Swift|year=2006|type=CD |publisher=[[Big Machine Records]]|id=BMR120702}}</ref> ''Taylor Swift'' was released on October 24, 2006.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/release/taylor-swift-mr0000686627|title=Taylor Swift \u2013 Taylor Swift |publisher=[[AllMusic]]|first=Jeff|last=Tamarkin|access-date=February 14, 2021}}</ref> The album peaked at number five on the U.S. [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]], where it spent 157 weeks\u2014the longest stay on the chart by any release in the U.S. in the 2000s decade.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last1=Trust |first1=Gary|title=Chart Beat Thursday: Taylor Swift, Tim McGraw Linked Again |date=October 29, 2009 |url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/266889/chart-beat-thursday-taylor-swift-tim-mcgraw-linked-again|access-date=November 8, 2016|magazine=Billboard|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130307153039/http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/266889/chart-beat-thursday-taylor-swift-tim-mcgraw-linked-again|archive-date=March 7, 2013|url-status=live}}</ref> It made Swift the first female country-music artist to write or co-write every track on a U.S. [[RIAA certification|platinum-certified]] album.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Taylor Swift |website=[[Songwriters' Hall of Fame]] |url=https://www.songhall.org/awards/winner/taylor_swift |access-date=September 21, 2022}}</ref>\n\nBig Machine Records was still in its infancy during the June 2006 release of the [[lead single]], \"[[Tim McGraw (song)|Tim McGraw]]\", which Swift and her mother helped promote by sending copies of the CD single to country radio stations.<ref name=\"EW1\">{{Cite magazine|last=Willman|first=Chris|title=Taylor Swift's Road to Fame|url=http://www.ew.com/article/2008/02/05/taylor-swifts-road-fame|magazine=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|access-date=April 22, 2012|page=3|date=February 5, 2008|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150221160659/http://www.ew.com/article/2008/02/05/taylor-swifts-road-fame|archive-date=February 21, 2015}}</ref> As there was not enough furniture at the label yet, they would sit on the floor to do so.<ref name=\"EW1\" /> She spent much of 2006 promoting ''Taylor Swift'' with a radio tour, television appearances, and opening for [[Rascal Flatts]] on select dates during their 2006 tour,<ref name=\"taylorjoinstour\">{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1543489/taylor-swift-joins-rascal-flatts-tour/|title=Taylor Swift Joins Rascal Flatts Tour|date=October 18, 2006|publisher=[[CMT (U.S. TV channel)|CMT]]|access-date=March 11, 2010|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150107133104/http://www.cmt.com/news/1543489/taylor-swift-joins-rascal-flatts-tour/|archive-date=January 7, 2015}}</ref> replacing [[Eric Church]], who had been fired for playing longer than his allotted time.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://tasteofcountry.com/eric-church-rascal-flatts-tour-taylor-swift-secret-history/|title=How Eric Church's Rascal Flatts Feud Helped Launch Taylor Swift's Career|first1=Sterling|last1=Whitaker|first2=Ania|last2=Hammar|work=Taste of Country|date=May 27, 2019|access-date=June 10, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190606114702/https://tasteofcountry.com/eric-church-rascal-flatts-tour-taylor-swift-secret-history/|archive-date=June 6, 2019|url-status=dead}}</ref> Borchetta said that although record industry peers initially disapproved of his signing a 15-year-old singer-songwriter, Swift tapped into a previously unknown market\u2014teenage girls who listen to country music.<ref name=\"EW1\" /><ref name=\"widdicombe1\" /> Following \"Tim McGraw\", four more singles were released throughout 2007 and 2008: \"[[Teardrops on My Guitar]]\", \"[[Our Song (Taylor Swift song)|Our Song]]\", \"[[Picture to Burn]]\" and \"[[Should've Said No]]\". All appeared on ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]''{{'}}s [[Hot Country Songs]], with \"Our Song\", and \"Should've Said No\" reaching number one. With \"Our Song\", Swift became the youngest person to single-handedly write and sing a number-one song on the chart.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.gactv.com/gac/cda/article_print/0,3008,GAC_26063_5769818_DS-ARTICLE-RIGHT-RAIL,00.html |title=Taylor Swift No. 1 on iTunes|date=December 19, 2007|publisher=[[Great American Country]]|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120303122404/http://www.gactv.com/gac/cda/article_print/0,3008,GAC_26063_5769818_DS-ARTICLE-RIGHT-RAIL,00.html|archive-date=March 3, 2012|access-date=July 5, 2010 |url-status=dead}}</ref> \"Teardrops on My Guitar\" reached number thirteen on the U.S. [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]].<ref name=\"chart history\" /> Swift also released two EPs, ''[[The Taylor Swift Holiday Collection]]'' in October 2007 and ''[[Beautiful Eyes]]'' in July 2008.<ref name=\"cst\">{{cite web|url=http://www.countrystandardtime.com/news/newsitem.asp?xid=1947|title=Taylor Swift owns top of country chart|access-date=December 26, 2008|date=July 23, 2008|work=[[Country Standard Time]]|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080731160355/http://www.countrystandardtime.com/news/newsitem.asp?xid=1947|archive-date=July 31, 2008|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref name=\"gac\">{{cite web|title=Wal-Mart \"Eyes\" New Taylor Swift Project|publisher=[[Great American Country]] |url=http://www.gactv.com/gac/nw_headlines/article/0,3034,GAC_26063_5903580_,00.html|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080723185436/http://www.gactv.com/gac/nw_headlines/article/0,3034,GAC_26063_5903580_,00.html|archive-date=July 23, 2008|access-date=July 24, 2008|url-status=dead}}</ref> She promoted her debut album extensively as the opening act for other country musicians' tours throughout 2006 and 2007, including [[George Strait]],<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1546137/taylor-swift-joins-george-straits-2007-tour/|title=Taylor Swift Joins George Strait's 2007 Tour|date=November 17, 2006|publisher=[[CMT (U.S. TV channel)|CMT]]|access-date=February 16, 2020}}</ref> [[Brad Paisley]],<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1549598/brad-paisley-plans-tour-with-three-opening-acts/ |title=Brad Paisley Plans Tour With Three Opening Acts|date=January 9, 2007|publisher=[[CMT (U.S. TV channel)|CMT]]|access-date=February 16, 2020}}</ref> and [[Tim McGraw]] and Faith Hill.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1561014/taylor-swift-joins-tim-mcgraw-faith-hill-on-tour/|title=Taylor Swift Joins Tim McGraw, Faith Hill on Tour|date=June 1, 2007|publisher=[[CMT (U.S. TV channel)|CMT]] |access-date=February 16, 2020}}</ref>\n\nSwift won multiple accolades for ''Taylor Swift''. She was one of the recipients of the [[Nashville Songwriters Association International|Nashville Songwriters Association]]'s Songwriter/Artist of the Year in 2007, becoming the youngest person to be honored with the title.<ref name=\":2\" /> She also won the [[Country Music Association]]'s Horizon Award for Best New Artist,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/pictures/taylor-swift/photo-gallery/2389485/2657043/artist_photo.jhtml|title=Photos : All Taylor Swift Pictures : Horizon Award Winner Poses in the Pressroom|publisher=[[CMT 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121113174555/http://www.cmt.com/pictures/taylor-swift/photo-gallery/2389485/2657043/artist_photo.jhtml|archive-date=November 13, 2012}}</ref> the [[Academy of Country Music Awards]]' Top New Female Vocalist,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/pictures/43rd-annual-acm-awards-onstage-winners/1587677/2970629/photo.jhtml|title=Photos : 43rd Annual ACM Awards \u2013 Onstage: Winners : Acceptance Speech|publisher=[[CMT (U.S. TV channel)|CMT]]|date=May 18, 2008|access-date=May 21, 2012}}</ref> and the [[American Music Awards]]' Favorite Country Female Artist honor.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.roughstock.com/blog/taylor-swift-rascal-flatts-carrie-underwood-score-@-2008-ama-awards|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140710055906/http://www.roughstock.com/blog/taylor-swift-rascal-flatts-carrie-underwood-score-%40-2008-ama-awards|archive-date=July 10, 2014|title=Taylor Swift, Rascal Flatts, Carrie Underwood Score at 2008 AMA Awards|publisher=Roughstock.com|type=Blog|date=November 24, 2008|access-date=May 21, 2012|url-status=dead}}</ref> She was also nominated for [[Grammy Award for Best New Artist|Best New Artist]] at the [[50th Annual Grammy Awards]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.people.com/people/package/article/0,,20173658_20177270,00.html|title=Amy Winehouse Wins Best New Artist, Kanye West Pays Tribute to Mom \u2013 Grammy Awards 2008, Grammy Awards|work=[[People (magazine)|People]]|date=October 2, 2008|access-date=May 21, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121113083832/http://www.people.com/people/package/article/0%2C%2C20173658_20177270%2C00.html|archive-date=November 13, 2012}}</ref> She opened for the Rascal Flatts on their 2008 summer and fall tour.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1586870/rascal-flatts-announce-summer-tour-with-taylor-swift/ |title=Rascal Flatts Announce Summer Tour With Taylor Swift |publisher=[[CMT (American TV channel)|CMT]] |date=May 5, 2008 |access-date=June 5, 2019}}</ref> In July of that year, Swift began dating singer [[Joe Jonas]], a relationship that ended three months later.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.people.com/people/article/0,,20230694,00.html|title=Scoop|last=Caplan|first=David|date=September 8, 2008|work=[[People (magazine)|People]]|access-date=March 6, 2012|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160202044308/http://www.people.com/people/article/0%2C%2C20230694%2C00.html|archive-date=February 2, 2016|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.people.com/people/article/0,,20245498,00.html|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160303204136/http://www.people.com/people/article/0%2C%2C20245498%2C00.html|archive-date=March 3, 2016|title=Scoop \u2013 Couples, Camilla Belle, Joe Jonas|last=Rizzo|first=Monica|date=November 24, 2008|work=[[People (magazine)|People]]|access-date=March 6, 2012|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\n=== 2008\u20132010: ''Fearless'' and acting debut ===\n[[File:TaylorSwiftApr09.jpg|thumb|upright|Swift at the 2009 premiere of ''[[Hannah Montana: The Movie]]''. She had a cameo appearance in the film and wrote two songs for [[Hannah Montana: The Movie (soundtrack)|its soundtrack]].<ref>{{Cite magazine|last1=Akers|first1=Shelley|title=Taylor Swift to Appear in Hannah Montana Movie|magazine=[[People (magazine)|People]]|date=June 9, 2008 |url=http://people.com/movies/taylor-swift-to-appear-in-hannah-montana-movie/|access-date=October 27, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171027181559/http://people.com/movies/taylor-swift-to-appear-in-hannah-montana-movie/|archive-date=October 27, 2017|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=\"hannah\" />|alt=Taylor Swift in 2009]]\nSwift's second studio album, ''[[Fearless (Taylor Swift album)|Fearless]]'', was released on November 11, 2008, in North America,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.umusicstore.com/cd-taylor-swift-fearless-cd-taylor-swift-fearless-1517/p|title=Taylor Swift \u2013 Fearless|publisher=[[Universal Music Group]]|language=pt|access-date=February 14, 2021|archive-date=January 18, 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210118071512/https://www.umusicstore.com/cd-taylor-swift-fearless-cd-taylor-swift-fearless-1517/p|url-status=dead}}</ref> and in March 2009, in other markets.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Raphael |first=Amy |date=February 1, 2009 |title=First, she conquered Nashville. Now she's set for world domination |url=https://www.proquest.com/docview/250507223 |url-access=subscription |access-date=2022-12-09 |website=[[The Observer]] |id={{ProQuest|250507223}}}}</ref> Five singles were released in 2008 through 2009: \"[[Love Story (Taylor Swift song)|Love Story]]\", \"[[White Horse (Taylor Swift song)|White Horse]]\", \"[[You Belong with Me]]\", \"[[Fifteen (song)|Fifteen]]\", and \"[[Fearless (Taylor Swift song)|Fearless]]\". \"Love Story\", the lead single, peaked at number four on the ''Billboard'' Hot 100 and number one in Australia.<ref name=\"chart history\" /><ref name=\"AUSchart\">{{cite web|url=http://australian-charts.com/showinterpret.asp?interpret=Taylor+Swift|title=Discography Taylor Swift|publisher=[[ARIA Charts]]|access-date=January 2, 2010|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120321080937/http://australian-charts.com/showinterpret.asp?interpret=Taylor+Swift|archive-date=March 21, 2012}}</ref> It was the first country song to top ''Billboard''<nowiki/>'s [[Mainstream Top 40|Pop Songs]] chart.<ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Trust |first=Gary |date=December 15, 2009 |title=Best of 2009: Part 1 |url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/266384/best-of-2009-part-1 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130303023328/http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/266384/best-of-2009-part-1 |archive-date=March 3, 2013 |access-date=September 20, 2022 |magazine=Billboard}}</ref> \"You Belong with Me\" was the album's highest-charting single on the ''Billboard'' Hot 100, peaking at number two,<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/267724/black-eyed-peas-jason-mraz-tie-records-on-billboard-hot-100|title=Black Eyed Peas, Jason Mraz Tie Records on Billboard Hot 100|last=Ben-Yehuda|first=Ayala|date=August 13, 2009|magazine=Billboard|access-date=March 13, 2010|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130508183109/http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/267724/black-eyed-peas-jason-mraz-tie-records-on-billboard-hot-100|archive-date=May 8, 2013}}</ref> and was the first country song to top ''Billboard''<nowiki/>'s all-genre [[Radio Songs (chart)|Radio Songs]] chart.<ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Trust |first=Gary |date=September 24, 2009 |title=Taylor Swift Climbs Hot 100, Black Eyed Peas Still No. 1 |url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/267297/taylor-swift-climbs-hot-100-black-eyed-peas-still-no-1 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130201055907/http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/267297/taylor-swift-climbs-hot-100-black-eyed-peas-still-no-1 |archive-date=February 1, 2013 |access-date=September 20, 2022 |magazine=Billboard}}</ref> All five singles were Hot Country Songs top-10 entries, with \"Love Story\" and \"You Belong with Me\" peaking at number one.<ref name=\"country songs\" /> ''Fearless'' debuted at number one on the ''Billboard'' 200 and was the top-selling album of 2009 in the U.S.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.yahoo.com/music/bp/chart-watch-extra-top-albums-last-10-years-181452729.html|title=Chart Watch Extra: Top Albums Of Last 10 Years|first=Paul|last=Grein|date=March 16, 2012|publisher=[[Yahoo! Music]]|type=Blog|access-date=June 10, 2011|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150402161744/https://www.yahoo.com/music/bp/chart-watch-extra-top-albums-last-10-years-181452729.html|archive-date=April 2, 2015}}</ref> The [[Fearless Tour]], Swift's first headlining concert tour, grossed over $63&nbsp;million.<ref>{{cite magazine|last=Mapes|first=Jillian|title=Taylor Swift Announces 'Speak Now' World Tour|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/photos/live/950374/taylor-swift-announces-speak-now-world-tour|magazine=Billboard|access-date=May 15, 2012|date=November 23, 2010|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130508182314/http://www.billboard.com/articles/photos/live/950374/taylor-swift-announces-speak-now-world-tour|archive-date=May 8, 2013}}</ref> ''[[Taylor Swift: Journey to Fearless|Journey to Fearless]]'', a three-part documentary miniseries, aired on television and was later released on DVD and Blu-ray.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Weiss|first1=Dan|title=Taylor Swift: Journey To Fearless DVD|url=http://americansongwriter.com/2011/12/taylor-swift-journey-to-fearless-dvd/|access-date=August 2, 2016|work=[[American Songwriter]]|date=December 12, 2011|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160815191946/http://americansongwriter.com/2011/12/taylor-swift-journey-to-fearless-dvd/|archive-date=August 15, 2016}}</ref> Swift also performed as a supporting act for [[Keith Urban]]'s Escape Together World Tour in 2009.<ref>{{cite web|last=Ryan|first=Sarah|url=http://blog.gactv.com/blog/2009/08/10/taylor-swift-pranks-keith-urban/|title=Taylor Swift Pranks Keith Urban|publisher=[[Great American Country]]|type=Blog|date=August Performance]]. It entered the Hot 100 at number three.<ref name=\"Billboard\">{{cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/956910/taylor-swift-makes-sparkling-hot-100-entrance|title=Taylor Swift Makes Sparkling Hot 100 Entrance|last=Pietroluongo|first=Silvio|date=August 11, 2010|magazine=Billboard|access-date=July 25, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160131095813/http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/956910/taylor-swift-makes-sparkling-hot-100-entrance|archive-date=January 31, 2016}}</ref> Swift wrote the album alone and co-produced every track.<ref name=\"NYT\">{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2010/10/24/arts/music/24swift.html|title=Taylor Swift, Angry on 'Speak Now'|last=Caramanica|first=Jon|work=[[The New York Times]]|date=October 20, 2010|access-date=October 23, 2010|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20101021050938/http://www.nytimes.com//2010//10//24//arts//music//24swift.html|archive-date=October 21, 2010}}</ref> ''Speak Now'', released on October 25, 2010,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1644093/taylor-swifts-new-album-speak-now-set-for-oct-25-release/|title=Taylor Swift's New Album, Speak Now, Set for Oct. 25 Release|date=July 20, 2010|publisher=[[CMT (U.S. TV channel)|CMT]]|access-date=February 14, 2020}}</ref> debuted atop the ''Billboard'' 200 with first-week sales of one million copies.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Kaufman|first1=Gil|title=Taylor Swift's Speak Now Tops 1 Million in First Week|url=http://www.mtv.com/news/1651391/taylor-swifts-speak-now-tops-1-million-in-first-week/|publisher=MTV|access-date=August 8, 2016|date=November 3, 2010|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160810044012/http://www.mtv.com/news/1651391/taylor-swifts-speak-now-tops-1-million-in-first-week/|archive-date=August 10, 2016}}</ref> It became the fastest-selling digital album by a female artist, with 278,000 downloads in a week, earning Swift an entry in the 2010 ''[[Guinness World Records]]''.<ref>{{Cite news|title=Fastest-selling digital album in the U.S. by a female artist|url=http://www.guinnessworldrecords.com/world-records/fastest-selling-digital-album-in-the-us-by-a-female-artist/|access-date=June 16, 2015|work=[[Guinness World 22, 2015}}</ref> The songs \"Mine\", \"[[Back to December]]\", \"[[Mean (Taylor Swift song)|Mean]]\", \"[[The Story of Us (song)|The Story of Us]]\", \"[[Sparks Fly (song)|Sparks Fly]]\", and \"[[Ours (song)|Ours]]\" were released as singles. All except \"The Story of Us\" were Hot Country Songs top-three entries, with \"Sparks Fly\" and \"Ours\" reaching number one.<ref name=\"country songs\">{{cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/taylor-swift/chart-history/csi/|title=Taylor Swift Chart History (Hot Country Songs)|magazine=Billboard|access-date=February 14, 2021}}</ref> \"Back to December\" and \"Mean\" peaked in the top ten in Canada.<ref name=\"canada\" /> Later in 2010, she briefly dated actor [[Jake Gyllenhaal]].<ref>{{cite 2012}}</ref>\n\nAt the [[54th Annual Grammy Awards]] in 2012, Swift won Best Country Song and [[Grammy Award for Best Country Solo Performance|Best Country Solo Performance]] for \"Mean\", which she It became her first number one in the U.S. and New Zealand,<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/480315/taylor-swift-scores-first-hot-100-no-1|title=Taylor Swift Scores First 2013}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Discography Taylor Swift|url=https://charts.nz/showinterpret.asp?interpret=Taylor+Swift|publisher=New Zealand Charts|access-date=July 26, 2016}}</ref> and reached the top slot on [[iTunes]]' digital song sales chart 50 minutes after its release, earning the Fastest Selling Single in Digital History Guinness World Record.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Lynch|first1=Kevin|title=Calvin Harris trumps Michael Jackson feat to join Taylor Swift, Rihanna and One Direction in Guinness World Records\u2122 2014 22, 2015}}</ref> Other singles released from the album include \"[[Begin Again (Taylor Swift song)|Begin Again]]\", \"[[I Knew You Were Trouble]]\", \"[[22 (Taylor Swift song)|22]]\", \"[[Everything Has Changed]]\", \"[[The Last Time (Taylor Swift song)|The Last Time]]\", and \"[[Red (Taylor Swift song)|Red]]\". \"I Knew You Were Trouble\" reached the top five on charts in Australia, Canada, Denmark, Ireland, New Zealand, the U.K. and the U.S.<ref>Chart positions:<br/>{{*}} {{cite ''Red'' was released on October 22, 2012.<ref>{{cite web Chapman and Liz Rose, as well as new producers such as [[Max Martin]] and [[Shellback (record producer)|Shellback]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/life/music/2012/10/17/taylor-swift-red-interview/1637307/|title=Taylor Swift sees 'Red' all over|first=Brian|last=Mansfield|date=October 17, 2012|work=[[USA incorporated many pop and rock styles such as [[heartland rock]], [[dubstep]] and [[dance-pop]].<ref name=\":17\">{{cite news |url=https://www.npr.org/2017/08/28/546359653/shocking-omissions-taylor-swift-s-red-a-canonical-coming-of-age-album|title=Taylor Swift's 'Red': A Canonical Coming-Of-Age Album|publisher=NPR|date=August 28, 2017|access-date=February 14, 2021|last1=English|first1=J.}}</ref> It debuted at number one on the ''Billboard'' 200 with first-week sales of 1.21&nbsp;million |url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/474400/taylor-swifts-red-sells-121-million-biggest-sales-week-for-an-album-since-2002|title=Taylor Swift's 'Red' Sells 1.21 Million; Biggest Sales Week for ''1989'' and ''Reputation'' ===\n[[File:Taylor Swift 045 (17682880264).jpg|thumb|upright|Swift at the [[1989 World Tour]], the highest-grossing tour of 2015]]\nIn March 2014, Swift began living in New York City.{{NoteTag|Though Swift has properties throughout the U.S., she identifies Nashville as her home.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.theatlantic.com/entertainment/archive/2014/03/taylor-swift-moves-into-nyc-apartment-built-over-mysterious-river-of-pink-slime/359891/|title=Taylor Swift Moves into NYC Apartment 27, 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://time.com/14933/taylor-swift-nashville-interview/|title=Why Taylor Swift Thinks Nashville Is the Best Place on Earth|first=Alex|last=Rogers|magazine=[[Time (magazine)|Time]]|date=March 7, 2014|access-date=September 27, 2016}}</ref>}} She worked on her fifth studio album, ''[[1989 (Taylor Swift album)|1989]]'', with producers Jack Antonoff, Max Martin, Shellback, [[Imogen Heap]], [[Ryan Tedder]], and [[Ali Payami]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.grammy.com/grammys/news/oral-history-taylor-swifts-1989|title=The Oral History of Taylor Swift's 1989|publisher=[[The Recording Academy]]|first=Paul|last=Zollo|date=February 17, 2016 |access-date=February 14, 2021}}</ref> She promoted the album through various campaigns, including inviting fans to secret album-listening sessions.<ref>{{cite magazine |url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/pop-shop/6288945/taylor-swift-1989-secret-sessions-behind-the-scenes-video|date=October 16, 2014|last=Stutz|first=Colin|access-date=August 2, 2016|title=Watch Taylor Swift's '1989' Secret Sessions Behind The Scenes Video |magazine=Billboard|url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160605172624/http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/pop-shop/6288945/taylor-swift-1989-secret-sessions-behind-the-scenes-video|archive-date=June 5, 2016}}</ref> The album was released on October 27, 2014, and debuted atop the U.S. ''Billboard'' 200 with sales of 1.28&nbsp;million copies in its first week.<ref>{{cite magazine|last=Caulfield|first=Keith |date=November 4, 2014|title=Taylor Swift's \"1989\" debuts with 1.287&nbsp;million copies sold 5, 2014 |access-date=November 4, 2014|magazine=Billboard}}</ref> Its singles \"[[Shake It Off]]\", \"[[Blank Space]]\" and \"[[Bad Blood (Taylor Swift song)|Bad Blood]]\" (featuring rapper [[Kendrick Lamar]]) reached number one in Australia, Canada and the U.S., the first two making Swift the first woman to replace herself at the top spot of the Hot 100.<ref>Chart positions:<br/>{{*}} {{cite web|title=Discography Taylor Swift|url=http://australian-charts.com/showinterpret.asp?interpret=Taylor+Swift|access-date=February 14, 2021|publisher=[[ARIA Charts]]}}<br/>{{*}} {{cite 2015}}</ref> The singles \"[[Style (Taylor Swift song)|Style]]\" and \"[[Wildest Dreams (Taylor Swift song)|Wildest Dreams]]\" reached the top 10 in the U.S.<ref>{{cite magazine|last=Trust|first=Gary |date=September 28, 2015|title=The Weeknd Holds Atop Hot 100, Taylor Swift Hits Top 10 With 'Wildest Dreams'|magazine=Billboard the Woods (song)|Out of the Woods]]\" and \"[[New Romantics (song)|New Romantics]]\".<ref name=\"US-singles\">{{Cite magazine|title=Taylor Swift \u2013 Chart History: Hot 100 |url={{BillboardURLbyName|artist=taylor swift|chart=Hot 100}}|access-date=September 18, 2016|magazine=Billboard}}</ref> [[The 1989 World Tour]] ran from May to December 2015 and was the highest-grossing tour of the year with $250&nbsp;million in total revenue.<ref>{{cite magazine|title=Live Music's $20 Billion Year: The Grateful Dead's Fare Thee Well Reunion, Taylor Swift, One 2015|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\nPrior to ''1989''{{'}}s release, Swift stressed the importance of albums to artists and fans.<ref name=\"Mann\">{{cite magazine|last1=Weissmann|first1=Jordan|title=Taylor Swift Has Written an Op-Ed in the Wall Street Journal |magazine=[[Slate (magazine)|Slate]]|type=Blog|date=July 7, 2014 |url=http://www.slate.com/blogs/moneybox/2014/07/07/taylor_swift_in_the_wall_street_journal_the_music_business_can_be_saved.html|access-date=January 23, 2015 |archive-date=January 23, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150123074145/http://www.slate.com/blogs/moneybox/2014/07/07/taylor_swift_in_the_wall_street_journal_the_music_business_can_be_saved.html|url-status=live }}</ref> In November 2014, she removed her entire catalog from [[Spotify]], arguing that the streaming company's ad-supported, free service undermined the premium service, which provides higher royalties for songwriters.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Knopper|first=Steve|title=Taylor Swift's Label Head Explains Spotify Removal |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/news/taylor-swift-scott-borchetta-spotify-20141108|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]] |date=November 8, 2014|access-date=April 11, 2015|url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150421045432/http://www.rollingstone.com/music/news/taylor-swift-scott-borchetta-spotify-20141108|archive-date=April 21, 2015}}</ref> In a June 2015 open letter, Swift criticized [[Apple Music]] for not offering royalties to artists during the streaming service's free three-month trial period and stated that she would pull ''1989'' from the catalog.<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/6605541/taylor-swift-pens-open-letter-explaining-why-1989-wont-be-on-apple-music|title=Taylor Swift Pens Open Letter 22, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> The following day, [[Apple Inc.]] announced that it would pay artists during the free trial period,<ref>{{cite magazine 2018, Swift featured on [[Sugarland]]'s \"[[Babe (Sugarland song)|Babe]]\" from their album ''[[Bigger (album)|Bigger]]''.{{NoteTag|Swift and [[Pat Monahan]] of [[Train (band)|Train]] originally wrote the song for Swift's 2012 album ''Red''.<ref name=\"Bigger\">{{cite magazine|last1=Hudak |first1=Joseph|title=Sugarland Announce New Album 'Bigger,' Taylor Swift Collaboration |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/country/news/sugarland-announce-new-album-bigger-taylor-swift-collaboration-w519097|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|access-date=April 13, 2018|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180414113840/https://www.rollingstone.com/country/news/sugarland-announce-new-album-bigger-taylor-swift-collaboration-w519097|archive-date=April 14, 2018}}</ref>}} In support of ''Reputation'', she embarked on her [[Taylor Swift's Reputation Stadium Tour|Reputation Stadium Tour]], which ran from May to November 2018.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Stubblebine|first=Allison |date=November 13, 2017 |title=Taylor Swift Announces First Round of Reputation Stadium Tour Dates |magazine=Billboard|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/pop/8031415/taylor-swift-reputation-tour-dates|access-date=November 18, 2017|url-status=live|archive-date=November 14, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171114063459/http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/pop/8031415/taylor-swift-reputation-tour-dates}}</ref> In the U.S., the tour grossed $266.1&nbsp;million in box office and sold over two million tickets, breaking Swift's own record for the highest-grossing U.S. tour by a woman, which was previously held by her 1989 World Tour in 2015 ($181.5&nbsp;million).<ref name=\"reputationtour\">{{cite magazine |last1=Frankenberg |first1=Eric |title=Taylor Swift's Reputation Stadium Tour Breaks Record for Highest-Grossing U.S. Tour |date=November 30, 2018 |magazine=Billboard |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/8487606/taylor-swift-reputation-stadium-tour-breaks-record-highest-grossing-us-tour |access-date=December 2, 2018 |archive-date=December 1, 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181201062855/https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/8487606/taylor-swift-reputation-stadium-tour-breaks-record-highest-grossing-us-tour}}</ref> It also broke the record for the highest-grossing North American concert tour in history. Worldwide, the tour grossed $345.7&nbsp;million,<ref>{{cite magazine|first=Eric|last=Frankenberg|date=December 6, 2018 |url=https://www.billboard.com/biz/articles/news/touring/8489131/taylor-swift-closes-reputation-stadium-tour-with-345-million|access-date=December 22, 2018|title=Taylor Swift Closes Reputation Stadium Tour with $345 Million |magazine=Billboard|url-status=live|archive-date=December 9, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181209172637/https://www.billboard.com/biz/articles/news/touring/8489131/taylor-swift-closes-reputation-stadium-tour-with-345-million}}</ref> making it the second highest-grossing concert tour of the year.<ref>{{cite news|first=Hugh|last=McIntyre|date=December 6, 2018 |url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/hughmcintyre/2018/12/06/these-are-the-10-highest-grossing-tours-of-2018/|title=These Are The 10 Highest-Grossing Tours of 2018|work=Forbes|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181207122741/https://www.forbes.com/sites/hughmcintyre/2018/12/06/these-are-the-10-highest-grossing-tours-of-2018/|archive-date=December 7, 2018|access-date=December 22, 2018}}</ref> On December 31, Swift released the tour's accompanying concert film on [[Netflix]].<ref>{{cite magazine |last1=Stiernberg |first1=Bonnie |title=Taylor Swift's 'Reputation' Hits Netflix: Twitter Reacts |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/8491775/taylor-swift-netflix-reputation-twitter-reaction |magazine=Billboard |date=December 31, 2018 |access-date=June 16, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190104085338/https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/8491775/taylor-swift-netflix-reputation-twitter-reaction|archive-date=January 4, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\n=== 2018\u20132020: ''Lover, Folklore'' and ''Evermore'' ===\n''Reputation'' was Swift's last album with Big Machine. In November 2018, she signed a new deal with the [[Universal Music Group]]; her subsequent releases were promoted by [[Republic Records]]. Swift said the contract included a provision for her to maintain ownership of her masters. In addition, in the event that Universal sold any part of its stake in Spotify, it agreed to distribute a non-recoupable portion of the proceeds among their artists.<ref>{{Cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/taylor-swift-universal-republic-deal-spotify-758102/|title=Taylor Swift's New Record Deal Affects Thousands of Other Musicians|last=Wang|first=Amy X.|date=November 19, 2018|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|access-date=November 26, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181126221710/https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/taylor-swift-universal-republic-deal-spotify-758102/|archive-date=November 26, 2018|url-status=live}}<br />{{Cite news|url=https://variety.com/2018/music/news/taylor-swift-stands-to-make-music-business-history-as-a-free-agent-1202918336/|title=Taylor Swift Stands to Make Music Business History as a Free Agent|last=Willman|first=Chris|date=August 27, 2018|work=Variety|access-date=August 29, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180829021649/https://variety.com/2018/music/news/taylor-swift-stands-to-make-music-business-history-as-a-free-agent-1202918336/|archive-date=August 29, 2018|url-status=live}}<br />{{cite news|url=https://variety.com/2018/music/news/taylor-swift-news-alert-1203032124/|title=Taylor Swift Signs New Deal With Universal Music 2018|last2=Willman|first2=Chris|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181119184301/https://variety.com/2018/music/news/taylor-swift-news-alert-1203032124/|archive-date=November 19, 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> [[Vox (website)|''Vox'']] called it a huge commitment from Universal, which was \"far from assured\" until Swift intervened.<ref>{{cite web|last=Grady|first=Constance|date=November 19, 2018|title=What Taylor Swift's new record deal means for the music industry \u2014 and for her image|url=https://www.vox.com/culture/2018/11/19/18102856/taylor-swift-record-deal-republic-records|access-date=December 20, 2021|website=Vox}}</ref>\n\n[[File:Taylor Swift 2 - 2019 by Glenn Francis (cropped) 3.jpg|thumb|upright|Swift at the [[2019 iHeartRadio Music Awards]]|alt=A portrait of Swift]]\nSwift released her seventh studio album, ''[[Lover (album)|Lover]]'', on August 23, 2019.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.npr.org/2019/08/23/753189805/stream-taylor-swifts-new-album-lover|title=Stream Taylor Swift's New Album, 'Lover'|first=Lyndsey|last=McKenna|publisher=[[NPR]]|date=August 23, 2019|access-date=September 10, 2019}}</ref> Besides Jack Antonoff, Swift worked with new producers [[Louis Bell]], [[Frank Dukes]], and [[Joel Little]].<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-album-reviews/taylor-swift-lover-875442/|title=Taylor Swift Reaches For New Heights of Personal and Musical Liberation on 'Lover'|first=Nick|last=Catucci|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=August 23, 2019|access-date=February 15, 2021}}</ref> ''Lover'' made Swift the first female artist to have a sixth consecutive album sell more than 500,000 copies in one week in the U.S.<ref name=\"BB200\">{{cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/8528870/taylor-swift-lover-album-debuts-at-no-1-on-billboard-200-chart|title=Official: Taylor Swift's 'Lover' Debuts at No. 1 on Billboard 200 Chart With 867,000 Units Earned in First Week in U.S.|first=Keith|last=Caulfield|magazine=Billboard |date=September 1, 2019|access-date=September 2, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190901210332/https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/8528870/taylor-swift-lover-album-debuts-at-no-1-on-billboard-200-chart|archive-date=September 1, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> The lead single, \"[[Me!]]\", debuted at number 100 on the ''Billboard'' Hot 100 and rose to number two a week later, scoring [[List of Billboard Hot 100 chart achievements and milestones#Biggest single-week upward movements|the biggest single-week jump]] in chart history.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/8510137/lil-nas-x-old-town-road-tops-hot-100-fifth-week|title=Lil Nas X's 'Old Town Road' Tops Billboard Hot 100 For Fifth Week, Taylor Swift's 'Me!' Vaults to No. 2|magazine=Billboard|last=Trust|first=Gary|date=May 6, 2019|access-date=June 14, 2019}}</ref> Other singles from ''Lover'' were the U.S. top-10 singles \"[[You Need to Calm Down]]\" and \"[[Lover (Taylor Swift song)|Lover]]\", and U.S. top-40 single \"[[The Man (Taylor Swift song)|The Man]]\".<ref name=\"chart history\" /> ''Lover'' was the world's best-selling album by a solo artist of 2019, selling 3.2&nbsp;million copies.<ref>{{cite magazine|date=March 19, 2020|title=Arashi Best-Of Tops Taylor Swift for IFPI's Best-Selling Album of 2019|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/international/9338380/ifpi-best-selling-albums-list-2019|magazine=Billboard|access-date=March 21, 2020}}</ref> The [[International Federation of the Phonographic Industry]] (IFPI) honored Swift as the global best-selling artist of 2019. Swift became first woman to win the honor twice, having previously won in 2014.<ref name=\":8\">{{Cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/business/9326226/taylor-swift-ifpi-global-best-selling-artist-2019|title=Taylor Swift Crowned IFPI's Global Best-Selling Artist|last=Cirisano|first=Tatiana|date=March 2, 2020|magazine=Billboard|access-date=March 2, 2020}}</ref> ''Lover'' and its singles earned nominations at the [[62nd Annual Grammy Awards]] in 2020.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.grammy.com/grammys/news/2020-grammy-awards-nominations-complete-winners-list|title=2020 Grammy Awards: Complete Winners List|date=November 20, 2019|publisher=[[The Recording Academy]]|access-date=February 15, 2021}}</ref> At the [[2019 MTV Video Music Awards]], \"Me!\" won [[MTV Video Music Award for Best Visual Effects|Best Visual Effects]], and \"You Need to Calm Down\" won Video of the Year and [[MTV Video Music Award for Best Video with a Social Message|Video for Good]]. Swift was the first female and second artist overall to win Video of the Year for a video that they directed.<ref>{{Cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/awards/8528396/12-records-2019-vma-awards|title=12 Records That Were Set at the 2019 VMAs|last=Grein|first=Paul|date=August 26, 2019|magazine=Billboard|access-date=January 11, 2020}}</ref>\n\nWhile promoting ''Lover'', Swift became embroiled in [[Taylor Swift masters controversy|a public dispute]] with talent manager [[Scooter Braun]] and Big Machine over the purchase of the masters of her back catalog.<ref name=\":7\">{{cite web |last=Grady |first=Constance |date=September 1, 2019 |title=The Taylor Swift/Scooter Braun controversy, explained |url=https://www.vox.com/culture/2019/7/1/20677241/taylor-swift-scooter-braun-controversy-explained |access-date=August 23, 2019 |website=[[Vox (website)|Vox]]}}</ref> Swift said she had been trying to buy the masters, but Big Machine only allowed her to do so if she exchanged one new album for each older one under another contract, which she refused to do.<ref name=\":7\" /><ref>{{Cite news |date=July 1, 2019 |title=The Taylor Swift, Scooter Braun, Justin Bieber row explained |work=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/newsbeat-48822388}}</ref> Swift began re-recording her back catalog in November 2020.<ref>{{cite magazine |last=Willman |first=Chris |date=November 16, 2020 |title=Taylor Swift Confirms Sale of Her Masters, Says She Is Already Re-Recording Her Catalog |url=https://variety.com/2020/music/news/taylor-swift-responds-scooter-brauns-sale-of-her-catalog-saying-1234833284/ |magazine=Variety |access-date=November 18, 2020}}</ref> Besides music, she played [[Bombalurina (cat)|Bombalurina]] in the [[Cats (2019 film)|movie adaptation]] of [[Andrew Lloyd Webber]]'s musical ''[[Cats (musical)|Cats]]'' (2019), for which she co-wrote and recorded the Golden Globe-nominated original song \"[[Beautiful Ghosts]]\".<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/8543715/taylor-swift-beautiful-ghosts-cat|title=Taylor Swift Releases 'Beautiful Ghosts,' Co-Written With Andrew Lloyd Webber for 'Cats' Film|last=Aniftos |first=Rania|magazine=Billboard|date=November 15, 2019|access-date=November 15, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|date=December 9, 2019|title=Golden Globes 2020: full list of nominations|newspaper=The Guardian 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191210105001/https://www.theguardian.com/film/2019/dec/09/golden-globes-2020-full-list-of-nominations|archive-date=December 10, 2019}}</ref> Critics panned the film but praised Swift's performance.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Rooney |first1=David |title='Cats': Film Review |url=https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/review/cats-review-1263550 |access-date=December 21, 2019 |work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]] |date=December 18, 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191220042249/https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/review/cats-review-1263550 |archive-date=December 20, 2019}}</ref> The documentary ''[[Miss Americana]]'', which chronicled parts of Swift's life and career, premiered at the [[2020 Sundance Film Festival]] and was released on [[Netflix]] that January.<ref name=\"billboard-20\">{{cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/movies/8548174/taylor-swift-miss-americana-netflix-documentary-release-date|title=Taylor Swift 'Miss Americana' Netflix Doc Has a Release Date & We're So Publishing Group]] in February 2020 after her 16-year-old contract with Sony/ATV expired.<ref>{{cite web |last=Willman |first=Chris |date=February 6, 2020 |title=Taylor Swift Moves to Universal Music Publishing Group with New Pact |url=https://variety.com/2020/music/news/taylor-swift-signs-umpg-publishing-deal-1203484798/ |access-date=February 6, 2020 |website=Variety}}</ref>\n\nAmidst the [[COVID-19 pandemic]], Swift released two [[surprise album]]s: ''[[Folklore (Taylor Swift album)|Folklore]]'' on July 24, and ''[[Evermore (Taylor Swift album)|Evermore]]'' on December 11, 2020.<ref>{{Cite news |last=Opperman|first=Jeff|date=March 12, 2021|title=Taylor Swift Is Singing Us Back to Nature|newspaper=[[The New York magazine |date=December 10, 2020|title=Taylor Swift to release surprise ninth album 'Evermore' tonight |url=https://www.nme.com/news/music/taylor-swift-to-release-surprise-ninth-album-evermore-tonight-2835851|access-date=December 10, 2020|magazine=[[NME]]}}</ref> Both explore [[indie folk]] and [[alternative rock]] with a more muted production compared to her previous upbeat pop songs.<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-features/aaron-dessner-interview-taylor-swift-evermore-1105853/|title=Aaron Dessner on How His Collaborative Chemistry With Taylor Swift Led to 'Evermore'|first=Claire |last=Schaffer|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=December 18, 2020|access-date=February 18, 2021}}</ref><ref name=\":15\" /> Swift wrote and recorded the albums with producers Jack Antonoff and [[Aaron Dessner]] from [[the National (band)|the National]].<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/pop/9423659/taylor-swift-folklore-review-first-listen|title=Taylor Swift's 'Folklore': There's Nothing Quiet About This Songwriting Tour De Force|last=Lipshutz|first=Jason|magazine=Billboard|date=July 24, 2020|access-date=July 24, 2020}}</ref> Alwyn co-wrote and co-produced select songs under the pseudonym William Bowery.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/pop/9500267/taylor-swift-joe-alwyn-songwriting-interview/|title=Taylor Swift Isn't So Sure She & Joe Alwyn Would Have Made Music Together If It Weren't for Lockdown |date=December 15, 2020|magazine=Billboard|first=Katie|last=Atkinson|access-date=February 18, 2021}}</ref> The albums were supported by three singles each, catering to the U.S. [[Contemporary hit radio|mainstream radio]], [[country radio]], and [[adult album alternative|triple A radio]]. The singles, in that order, were \"[[Cardigan (song)|Cardigan]]\", \"[[Betty (Taylor Swift song)|Betty]]\", and \"[[Exile (Taylor Swift song)|Exile]]\" from ''Folklore,'' and \"[[Willow (song)|Willow]]\", \"[[No Body, No Crime]]\", and \"[[Coney Island (Taylor Swift song)|Coney Island]]\" from ''Evermore''.<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/9517376/taylor-swift-evermore-radio-rollout/ |title=Taylor Swift's 'Coney Island' and 'No Body, No Crime' Debut on Airplay Charts, Joining 'Willow' |first=Gary|last=Trust|date=January 28, 2021|magazine=Billboard|access-date=February 2, 2021}}</ref> Swift became the first artist to debut a U.S. number-one album and a number-one song at the same time with ''Folklore''<nowiki/>'s \"Cardigan\" and ''Evermore''<nowiki/>'s \"Willow\".<ref>{{cite magazine |date=December 21, 2020|title=Taylor Swift's 'Willow' Debuts at No. 1 on Billboard Hot 100 |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/9503448/taylor-swift-willow-debut-number-one-hot-100/ |magazine=Billboard|access-date=February 18, 2021}}</ref> ''Folklore'' was 2020's best-selling album in the U.S. with 1.2&nbsp;million copies.<ref name=\"jan212\">{{cite magazine|last=Caulfield |first=Keith|date=January 7, 2021 |title=Lil Baby's 'My Turn' Is MRC Data's Top Album of 2020, Roddy Ricch's 'The Box' Most-Streamed Song|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/9508037/mrc-data-2020-recap/|access-date=January 7, 2021 |magazine=Billboard}}</ref> It won Album of the Year at the [[63rd Annual Grammy Awards]], making Swift the first woman to win the award thrice.<ref name=\"folklorevariety\">{{cite web |last=Willman |first=Chris |date=March 14, 2021 |title=Taylor Swift Becomes First Woman to Win Album of the Year Grammy Three Times |url=https://variety.com/2021/music/news/taylor-swift-grammys-album-of-year-first-woman-three-times-folklore-1234930200/ |access-date=March 15, 2021 |website=Variety}}</ref> At the [[American Music Awards of 2020|2020 American Music Awards]], Swift won three awards, including Artist of the Year for a record third consecutive time.<ref>{{Cite magazine |last1=Willman |first1=Chris |date=November 23, 2020 |title=Taylor Swift Wins Three American Music Awards, Says She's MIA Because of 'Recording All of My Old Music' |url=https://variety.com/2020/music/news/taylor-swift-wins-three-american-music-awards-says-shes-mia-because-of-recording-all-of-my-old-music-1234837818/ |magazine=Variety |access-date=November 25, 2020}}</ref> She was 2020's highest-paid musician in the U.S., and the world's highest-paid solo musician.<ref>{{cite magazine|last=Christman |first=Ed|date=July 19, 2021|title=Billboard's U.S. Money Makers: The Top Paid Musicians of 2020 |magazine=Billboard |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/9602078/musician-us-money-makers-highest-paid-2020/|access-date=July 19, 2021}}<br/>{{*}} {{Cite |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/money-makers/9602829/musician-global-money-makers-highest-paid-2020-report|access-date=July 19, 2021|magazine=Billboard}}</ref>\n\n===2021\u2013present: Re-recordings and ''Midnights''===\n[[File:HAIMO2210722 (31 of 51) (52233070660) Cropped.jpg|thumb|upright|Swift as a surprise guest on the [[One More Haim Tour]] (2022)]]\n\nFollowing the masters dispute, Swift released two [[re-recording (music)|re-recorded]] albums in 2021, adding \"Taylor's Version\" to their titles. The first, ''[[Fearless (Taylor's Version)]]'', peaked atop the ''Billboard'' 200, becoming the first re-recorded album to do so.<ref>{{cite magazine |last1=Caulfield |first1=Keith |title=Taylor Swift's Re-Recorded 'Fearless' Album Debuts at No. 1 on Billboard 200 Chart With Year's Biggest Week |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/9558306/taylor-swift-fearless-taylors-version-tops-billboard-200/ |magazine=Billboard |access-date=April 19, 2021 |date=April 18, 2021}}</ref> It was preceded by the three tracks: \"[[Love Story (Taylor's Version)]]\", \"[[You All Over Me]]\" with [[Maren Morris]], and \"[[Mr. Perfectly Fine]]\",<ref>{{cite magazine|last=Shaffer|first=Claire|date=April 7, 2021|title=Taylor Swift Releases New 'Fearless' Vault Song 'Mr. Perfectly Fine'|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/taylor-swift-fearless-vault-song-1152044/|access-date=April 7, 2021|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|url-access=limited|archive-date=April 10, 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210410125905/https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/taylor-swift-fearless-vault-song-1152044/|url-status=live}}</ref> the first of which made Swift the second artist after [[Dolly Parton]] to have both the original and the re-recording of a single reach number one on the Hot Country Songs chart.<ref>{{Cite magazine|title=Taylor Swift's 'Love Story (Taylor's Version)' Debuts at No. 1 on Hot Country Songs Chart: 'I'm So Grateful to the Fans'|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/9529564/taylor-swift-love-story-number-one-hot-country-songs/|access-date=February 22, 2021|magazine=Billboard|date=February 22, 2021|first1=Jim|last1=Asker|first2=Gary|last2=Trust}}</ref> The second re-recording ''[[Red (Taylor's Version)]]'' was released on November 12.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Al-Heeti|first=Abrar|date=October 28, 2021|title=Red (Taylor's Version): Release date, tracklist and why Taylor Swift is rerecording her albums|publisher=CNET|url=https://www.cnet.com/news/red-taylors-version-release-date-tracklist-and-why-taylor-swift-is-rerecording-her-albums/|access-date=October 30, 2021}}</ref> Its final track, \"[[All Too Well (10 Minute Version)]]\"\u2014accompanied by [[All Too Well: The Short Film|the namesake short film]] directed by Swift\u2014debuted at number one on the Hot 100, becoming the longest song in history to top the chart.<ref>{{cite web|date=November 26, 2021|title=Taylor Swift's 10-minute 'All Too Well' is longest song to reach No.1|url=https://www.guinnessworldrecords.com/news/2021/11/taylor-swifts-10-minute-all-too-well-is-longest-song-to-reach-no-1-683614|access-date=November 26, 2021|website=[[Guinness World Records]]}}</ref> She was the highest-paid female musician of 2021,<ref>{{cite magazine|magazine=Rolling Stone|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-lists/highest-paid-musicians-2021-bruce-springsteen-jay-z-taylor-swift-1281654/taylor-swift-80-million-1282542/|title=Nine of the 10 Highest-Paid Musicians of 2021 Were Men|date=January 14, 2022|access-date=January 14, 2021}}</ref> and both her 2020 albums and the re-recordings were ranked among the top 10 best-sellers of the year.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Caulfield|first=Keith|date=January 6, 2022|title=Dua Lipa's 'Levitating' Is Most-Streamed Song of 2021 In U.S., Morgan Wallen's 'Dangerous: The Double Album' Is MRC Data's Top Album|url=https://www.billboard.com/music/chart-beat/dua-lipa-morgan-wallen-us-2021-mrc-data-1235016079/|access-date=January 17, 2022|magazine=Billboard}}</ref> In May 2021, Swift was awarded the [[Brit Award for Outstanding Contribution to Music|Global Icon Award]] by the Brit Awards<ref name=\":12\" /> and the Songwriter Icon Award by the [[National Music Publishers' Association]].<ref>{{cite news|date=May 24, 2021|title=NMPA to honor Taylor Swift with Songwriter Icon Award among other 2021 annual meeting honorees|url=https://www.nmpa.org/nmpa-to-honor-taylor-swift-with-songwriter-icon-award-among-other-2021-annual-meeting-honorees/|access-date=May 24, 2021|agency=[[National Music Publishers' Association]]}}</ref> Swift further released \"[[Wildest Dreams (Taylor's Version)]]\" on September 17, 2021, and \"[[This Love (Taylor's Version)]]\" on May 6, 2022.<ref>{{Cite magazine |title=Swifties Are Freaking Out About 'Wildest Dreams (Taylor's Version),' But Wonder 'What Era Are We In?' |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/pop/9631866/wildest-dreams-taylors-version-reactions-what-era-are-we-in/ |magazine=Billboard |access-date=September 18, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine magazine|last=Cohen|first=Jonathan |date=June 29, 2021|title=Aaron Dessner, Justin Vernon Rev Up Big Red Machine With Help From Taylor \"[[Gasoline (Haim song)|Gasoline]]\"<ref>{{cite web|last=Strauss|first=Matthew|date=February 19, 2021|title=HAIM Enlist Taylor Swift for New \"Gasoline\" \"[[Carolina (Taylor Swift song)|Carolina]]\" as part of the soundtrack of the film ''[[Where the Crawdads Sing (film)|Where the Crawdads Sing]]'',<ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Blistein |first=Jon |date=March 22, 2022 |title=Taylor Swift Teases New Song 'Carolina' in 'Where the Crawdads Sing' Trailer the period comedy ''[[Amsterdam (2022 film)|Amsterdam]]''.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Utley |first=Riley |date=October 13, 2022 |title=Every Taylor Swift Movie Performance, Ranked |url=https://www.cinemablend.com/movies/every-taylor-swift-movie-performance-ranked |access-date=October 14, 2022 |website=[[CinemaBlend]]}}</ref> She received four nominations at the [[65th Annual Grammy Awards]], including \"All Too Well (10 Minute Version)\" for Song of the Year and \"Carolina\" for Best Song Written for Visual Media.<ref name=\":31\" />\n\nSwift won three awards at the [[2022 MTV Video Music Awards]], including [[MTV Video Music Award for Video of the Year|Video of the Year]] (for ''All Too Well: The Short Film'') for a record-breaking third time.<ref name=\"vmarecord\">{{Cite news |last=Corcoran |first=Nina |date=August 28, 2022 |title=Taylor Swift Announces New Album ''Midnights'', Breaks Record for Most Video of the Year Wins at 2022 VMAs her tenth studio album, ''[[Midnights]]'', which was released on October 21.<ref>{{cite magazine |last1=Huff |first1=Lauren |title=Taylor Swift reveals 7 more songs after ''Midnights'' release pop on the album,<ref>{{Cite news |date=October 21, 2022 |title=Taylor Swift reveals late-night musings on pop album 'Midnights' |work=Reuters |url=https://www.theguardian.com/music/2022/oct/22/taylor-swifts-new-album-breaks-spotify-streaming-record |access-date=October 22, 2022}}</ref> and [[chill-out music]].<ref name=\":102\">{{Cite news |last=Powers |first=Ann |author-link=Ann Powers |date=October 21, 2022 |title=In the haze of 'Midnights,' Taylor Swift softens into an expanded sound |agency=[[NPR]] |url=https://www.npr.org/2022/10/21/1130293117/midnights-taylor-swift-review |access-date=October 21, 2022}}</ref> Breaking a string of records,<ref name=\":31\">{{Cite magazine |last=Dailey |first=Hannah |date=December 6, 2022 |title=Here Are All of Taylor Swift's Biggest Accomplishments in 2022 |url=https://www.billboard.com/lists/taylor-swift-biggest-accomplishments-2022/ |access-date=December 7, 2022 |magazine=Billboard}}</ref> ''Midnights'' and its lead single, \"[[Anti-Hero (song)|Anti-Hero]]\", became [[List of most-streamed songs on Spotify|Spotify's most-streamed album and song in one day]] with 185{{nbsp}}million and 17.4{{nbsp}}million plays, respectively.<ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Shafer |first=Ellise |date=October 21, 2022 |title=Taylor Swift's 2022 in the US, ''Midnights'' debuted atop the ''Billboard'' 200 with 1.57{{nbsp}}million units and marked Swift's fifth album to open with over one million copies sold. She tied [[Barbra Streisand]] for the most number-one albums among women (11). Swift became the first artist to occupy the Hot 100's entire top 10, with \"Anti-Hero\" at the top.<ref name=\":31\" /> In support of ''Midnights'' and her previous albums, Swift will embark on [[the Eras Tour]] (2023), which broke the record for most concert tickets ever sold in a single day.<ref name=\":31\" /> However, [[Ticketmaster]] was [[2022 Ticketmaster controversy|widely castigated]] for handling the tour's presale poorly, triggering government investigations into the company.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Mahdawi |first=Arwa |date=November 20, 2022 |title=Swifties know: the Ticketmaster \"until a later date\".<ref name=\":32\">{{cite news |url=https://variety.com/2022/film/news/taylor-swift-feature-directing-debut-searchlight-pictures-1235455606/ |title=Taylor Swift Making Feature Directing Debut for Searchlight Pictures |date=December 9, 2022 |access-date=December 9, 2022 |work=Variety |last=Lang |first=Brent}}</ref>\n\n== Artistry ==\n=== Influences ===\n{{multiple image\n| 153\n| align     = left\n}}\n\nOne of Swift's earliest memories of music is listening to her grandmother, [[Marjorie Finlay]], sing in church.{{sfn|Jepson|2013|p=1}} As a child, she enjoyed [[The Walt Disney Company|Disney]] film soundtracks: \"My parents noticed that, once I had run out of words, I would just make up my own.\"<ref name=\"theaustralian1\">{{Cite news|first=Dan|last=Cairns|date=March 5, 2009|newspaper=[[The Australian]] |url=http://www.theaustralian.com.au/arts/swift-rise-of-the-anti-diva/story-e6frg8n6-1111119032411 the anti-diva|access-date=July 2, 2012}}</ref> Swift said she owes her confidence to her mother, who helped her prepare for class presentations as a child.<ref>{{cite web|last=Bream|first=Jon|date=December 7, 2007|title=Music: OMG! Taylor's senior year|work=[[Star Tribune]] |url=http://www.startribune.com/omg-taylor-s-senior-year/12149446/?elr=KArks%3ADCiU1PciUiD3aPc%3A_Yyc%3AaUoaEYY_1Pc_bDaEP7U|access-date=July 1, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> She also attributes her \"fascination with writing and storytelling\" to her mother.<ref name=\"sessionsinterview\" /> Swift was drawn to the storytelling aspect of country music,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.countrystandardtime.com/news/newsitem.asp?xid=4649|title=Swift starts world tour in Asia, pushes \"Speak Now' in NY|date=October 23, 2007|website=[[Country 2012}}</ref> and was introduced to the genre listening to \"the great female country artists\" of the 1990s\u2014Shania Twain, Faith Hill, and the Dixie Chicks.<ref name=\"CMT 2007-11-12\">{{cite web |url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1574118/20-questions-with-taylor-swift/|title=News : 20 Questions With Taylor Swift|date=November 12, 2007|publisher=[[Country Music Television|CMT]]|access-date=April 18, 2012|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121114113840/http://159.54.226.237/08_issues/080413/080413taylor-swift.html}}</ref> Twain, both as a songwriter and performer, was her biggest musical influence.<ref>{{Cite magazine |url=http://content.time.com/time/magazine/article/0,9171,1893502-1,00.html |title=Interview with Taylor Swift|magazine=[[Time (magazine)|Time]]|date=April 23, often imitate her.<ref>{{Cite news|title=Taylor Swift Style: Singer Won't Take Her Clothes Off, Wants People To Focus On 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> She admired the Dixie Chicks' defiant attitude and their ability to play their own instruments.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.instyle.co.uk/celebrity/news/instyle-meets-country-singing-sensation-taylor-swift|title=InStyle meets country singing sensation Taylor Swift|work=[[InStyle UK]]|date=October 26, \"[[Kiss Me (Sixpence None the Richer song)|Kiss Me]]\" by [[Sixpence None the Richer]] was the first song Swift learned to play on the guitar.<ref>{{cite web|author=The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon|date=October 4, 2019 |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hQH6bv946T4&t=215s| archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/varchive/youtube/20211029/hQH6bv946T4| url-status=live |archive-date=October [[Patsy Cline]], [[Loretta Lynn]], [[Tammy Wynette]], and [[Dolly Parton]],<ref name=\"Rolling Stone 2008-12-08\"/> the last of whom she believes is exemplary to female songwriters,<ref name=\"billboard2\"/> and [[alt-country]] artists like [[Patty Griffin]]<ref>{{cite web|title=Taylor Swift's Favorite Music |work=[[The Oprah Winfrey Show]]|url=http://www.oprah.com/entertainment/Taylor-Swifts-Favorite-Music |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160116064914/http://www.oprah.com/entertainment/Taylor-Swifts-Favorite-Music |archive-date=January 16, 2016|access-date=October 23, 2012}}</ref> and [[Lori McKenna]].<ref name=\"widdicombe1\" /> As a songwriter, Swift was influenced by [[Joni Mitchell]], citing especially how Mitchell's autobiographical lyrics convey the deepest emotions; \"I think [''[[Blue (Joni Mitchell album)|Blue]]''] is my favorite because it explores somebody's soul so deeply.\"<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-lists/joni-mitchell-15-great-artists-influenced-by-the-blue-singer-168972/taylor-swift-30-154837/|title=Joni Mitchell: 15 Great Artists Influenced by the 'Blue' Singer|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=June 22, 2016|access-date=December 26, 2020}}</ref>\n\nSwift has also been influenced by various pop and rock artists. McCartney, both as a member of [[the Beatles]] and a soloist, makes Swift feel \"as if I've been let into his heart and his mind&nbsp;[...] He's out there continuing to make his fans so happy.\"<ref>{{cite web|title=Rolling in the Trophies? \u2013 Adele|url=http://www.people.com/people/archive/article/0,,20567076,00.html|work=[[People (magazine)|People]]|date=February 6, on my career.\"<ref>{{Cite web |date=June 4, 2013 |title=The Rolling Stones & Taylor Swift \u2013 As Tears Go By \u2013 Live in Chicago |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=O52TbIbCEKo |access-date=October 24, 2022 |website=The Rolling Stones |via=YouTube}}</ref> As she grows older, Swift aspires to be like Harris and prioritize music over fame.<ref>{{cite says that Kristofferson \"shines in songwriting\",<ref name=\"single life\">{{Cite news|last=Van Meter|first=Jonathan|url=http://www.vogue.com/865383/taylor-swift-the-single-life/#1|title=Taylor being emotional but \"strong\" at the same time.<ref name=\":3\">{{Cite news|url=http://www.news.com.au/entertainment/music/taylor-swift-is-happy-to-be-your-break-up-musician/story-e6frfn09-1226644234716|title=Taylor Swift is happy to be your break-up musician 19, 2013|url-status=live}}</ref> Her synth-pop album ''1989'' was influenced by some of her favorite 1980s pop acts, including [[Peter Gabriel]], [[Annie Lennox]], [[Phil Collins]], and Madonna.<ref name=\"NPR Music\">{{cite interview|format=Audio upload and transcript|interviewer=Melissa Block |subject=Taylor Swift
