major influences.<ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Hiatt |first=Brian |date=June 18, 2019 |title=Taylor Swift: The Rolling Stone Interview |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-features/taylor-swift-rolling-stone-interview-880794/ |access-date=April 14, 2022 |magazine=Rolling Stone}}</ref>\n\n=== Musical styles ===\n{{Quote box |salign=center |width=20em |align=right |quote=\"If there's one thing that Swift has proven throughout her career, it's that she refuses to be put in a box. Her ever-evolving sound took her from country darling to pop phenom to folk's newest raconteur.\"|source=\u2014[[The Recording Academy]], 2021<ref>{{cite web|last=Weatherby|first=Taylor|date=March 10, 2021|title=Taylor Swift's Road to ''Folklore''|url=https://www.grammy.com/grammys/news/taylor-swift-folklore-2021-grammys|access-date=November 24, 2021|publisher=[[The Recording Academy]]}}</ref>}}\n\nSwift is known for venturing into various music genres,<ref name=\":32\" /> having been described as a \"music [[chameleon]]\".<ref>{{Cite news |last=Savage |first=Mark |date=October 19, 2022 |title=Midnights: What we know about Taylor Swift's songwriting|publisher=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/entertainment-arts-63233361 |access-date=October 20, 2022}}</ref><ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Bruner |first=Raisa |date=August 24, 2020 |title=Let's Break Down Taylor Swift's Tender New Album Folklore |url=https://time.com/5871159/taylor-swift-folklore-explained/ |access-date=October 20, 2022 |magazine=Time}}</ref> She self-identified as a country musician until 2012, when she released her fourth studio album, ''Red''.{{sfn|McNutt|2020|p=77}} Her albums were promoted to country radio, but music critics noted wide-ranging styles of pop and rock.{{sfnm|1a1=Hughes|1y=2017|1p=206|2a1=Perone|2y=2017|2p=33}}<ref>{{cite magazine|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121205103736/http://www.rollingstone.com/music/artists/taylor-swift/albumguide|url=http://www.rollingstone.com/music/artists/taylor-swift/albumguide|title=Taylor Swift: Album Guide|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|archive-date=December 5, 2012|url-status=dead|access-date=December 5, 2012}}</ref> After 2010, they observed that Swift's melodies are rooted in pop music, and the country music elements are limited to instruments such as banjo, [[mandolin]], and [[fiddle]], and her slight [[twang]];<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2011/07/22/arts/music/pop-and-rock-listings-july-22-28.html|title=Pop and Rock Listings July 22 \u2013 28|date=July 21, 2011|newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=July 12, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120128232427/http://www.nytimes.com/2011/07/22/arts/music/pop-and-rock-listings-july-22-28.html|archive-date=January 28, 2012}}</ref><ref name=\":02\"/> some commented that her country music identity was an indicator of her narrative songwriting rather than musical style.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.theguardian.com/music/2009/mar/06/taylor-swift-fearless-album-review |title=Taylor Swift: ''Fearless''|first=Alexis|last=Petridis|author-link=Alexis Petridis|website=The Guardian|date=March 6, 2009|access-date=August 13, 2022}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2008/11/10/prodigy-pop-music-sasha-frere-jones|title=Prodigy |first=Sasha-Frere|last=Jones|author-link=Sasha Frere-Jones|magazine=[[The New Yorker]]|date=November 11, 2008|access-date=August 14, 2022}}</ref> Although the Nashville music industry was receptive of Swift's status as a country musician, critics accused her of abandoning the legitimate roots of country music in favor of [[crossover music|crossover]] success in the mainstream pop market.{{sfn|Hughes|2017|p=206}}<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://americansongwriter.com/taylor-swift-the-garden-in-the-machine/5/|title=Taylor Swift: The Garden In The Machine|first=Jim|last=Malec|work=[[American Songwriter]]|date=May 2, 2011|page=5|access-date=August 12, 2022}}</ref> ''Red''{{'s}} eclectic pop, rock, and [[electronic music|electronic]] styles intensified the critical debate, to which Swift responded, \"I leave the genre labeling to other people.\"{{sfn|McNutt|2020|p=78}}\n\nMusic journalist [[Jody Rosen]] commented that by originating her musical career in Nashville, Swift made a \"bait-and-switch maneuver{{Nbsp}}... planting roots in loamy country soil, then pivoting to pop\".<ref name=\"Rosen\"/> She abandoned her country-music identity in 2014, when she released her synth-pop fifth studio album, ''1989'', which she described as her first \"documented, official pop album\".{{sfn|McNutt|2020|p=79}} Her albums ''Reputation'' (2017) and ''Lover'' (2019) have an upbeat pop production; the former incorporates [[hip hop music|hip hop]] and [[trap music|trap]] elements.<ref name=\"Levine\"/><ref name=\":19\">{{cite web|last=da Silva|first=Michelle|date=November 13, 2017|title=Taylor Swift Has Changed for the Worse on ''Reputation''|url=https://nowtoronto.com/music/album-reviews/taylor-swift-bad-reputation|access-date=July 27, 2020|website=[[Now (newspaper)|Now]]}}</ref> Although reviews of Swift's pop albums were generally positive, critics lamented that the pop music production indicated Swift's pursuit of mainstream success, which eroded her authenticity as a songwriter nurtured by her country music background.{{sfnm|1a1=McNutt|1y=2020|1p=79|2a1=Sloan|2y=2021|2p=17}} [[Musicologist]] Nate Sloan remarked that Swift's pop music transition was rather motivated by her need to expand her artistry.{{sfn|Sloan|2021|p=17}} Swift eschewed mainstream pop in favor of [[Alternative music|alternative]] styles like [[indie rock]] with her 2020 studio albums, ''Folklore'' and ''Evermore''.<ref name=\"Indie rock\" /><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/07/26/arts/music/taylor-swift-folklore-review.html|title=Taylor Swift, A Pop Star Done with Pop|first=Jon|last=Caramanica|author-link=Jon Caramanica|website=[[The New York Times]]|url-access=limited|date=July 26, 2020|access-date=August 14, 2022}}</ref> ''[[Clash (magazine)|Clash]]'' said her career \"has always been one of transcendence and covert boundary-pushing\", reaching a point at which \"Taylor Swift is just Taylor Swift\", not defined by any genre.<ref name=\":23\">{{cite web|last=Harbron|first=Lucy|date=November 11, 2021|title=Why Taylor Swift's 'Red' Is Her Turning Point|url=https://www.clashmusic.com/features/why-taylor-swifts-red-is-her-turning-point|access-date=November 12, 2021|website=Clash}}</ref>\n\n===Voice===\nSwift possesses a [[mezzo-soprano]] [[Voice type|vocal range]],{{sfn|Fulford|2014|p=192}} and a generally soft [[timbre]].<ref>{{Cite magazine |date=December 11, 2020 |title=Taylor Swift Deepens Her Goth-Folk Vision on the Excellent 'Evermore' |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-album-reviews/taylor-swift-evermore-folklore-1101778/ |access-date=August 23, 2022 |magazine=Rolling Stone}}</ref> During her career as a country singer, her vocals were criticized by some as weak and strained compared to those of her contemporaries.{{sfn|Provenzano|2018|p=173}} Swift admitted her vocal ability often concerned her in her early career, and has worked hard to improve.<ref name=\"Up for Discussion\">{{cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/953737/taylor-swift-the-billboard-cover-story|title=Taylor Swift: The ''Billboard'' Cover Story|last=Roland|first=Tom|date=October 15, 2010|magazine=Billboard|access-date=July 3, 2012|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20101018200303/http://www.billboard.com/features/taylor-swift-the-billboard-cover-story-1004121338.story|archive-date=October 18, 2010|url-status=dead}}</ref> After transitioning to pop music with ''1989'', reviews of her vocals remained mixed; critics complained that she lacks proper technique but appreciated her usage of her voice to communicate her feelings to the audience, prioritizing \"intimacy over power and nuance\".{{sfn|Provenzano|2018|pp=173\u2013174}} They also praised her for refraining from correcting her [[pitch (music)|pitch]] with [[Auto-Tune]].{{sfn|Provenzano|2018|p=174}} ''Los Angeles Times'' music critic [[Ann Powers]] remarked in 2010 that Swift's defining vocal feature is her attention to detail to convey an exact feeling\u2014\"the line that slides down like a contented sigh or up like a raised eyebrow\".<ref name=\"LAT\">{{Cite news|url=http://latimesblogs.latimes.com/music_blog/2010/10/album-review-taylor-swifts-speak-now.html |title=Album review: Taylor Swift's ''Speak Now''|last=Powers|first=Ann|author-link=Ann Powers |date=October 25, 2010|work=[[Los Angeles Times]]|access-date=October 25, 2010|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20101028003032/http://latimesblogs.latimes.com/music_blog/2010/10/album-review-taylor-swifts-speak-now.html|archive-date=October 28, 2010}}</ref>\n\nReviews of Swift's later albums were more appreciative of her vocals, finding them less nasal, richer, and more resonant.<ref name=\":02\">{{cite news|date=April 9, 2021|title=Taylor Swift Remade ''Fearless'' as ''Taylor's Version''. Let's Discuss.|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/09/arts/music/taylor-swift-fearless-taylors-version.html|url-status=live|url-access=limited|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210409224903/https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/09/arts/music/taylor-swift-fearless-taylors-version.html|archive-date=April 9, 2021|access-date=April 21, 2021|newspaper=[[The New York Times]]}}</ref><ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Barker|first=Andrew|date=November 27, 2020|title=''Folklore: The Long Pond Studio Sessions'' Review|url=https://variety.com/2020/film/reviews/folklore-the-long-pond-studio-sessions-film-review-taylor-swift-1234840985/|access-date=May 31, 2021|magazine=Variety}}</ref> With ''Folklore'' and ''Evermore,'' critics complimented her sharp and agile yet translucent and controlled vocals.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Kornhaber |first=Spencer |date=July 28, 2020 |title=Taylor Swift Is No Longer Living in the Present |url=https://www.theatlantic.com/culture/archive/2020/07/taylor-swift-folklore-review-power-storytelling/614698/ |access-date=August 23, 2022 |website=The Atlantic}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Brehian |first=Tom |date=July 24, 2020 |title=Review: Taylor Swift's 'folklore' Is An Indie Record Unconcerned With Being Cool |url=https://www.stereogum.com/2092670/taylor-swift-folklore-review/reviews/premature-evaluation/ |access-date=August 23, 2022 |website=[[Stereogum]]}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Willman |first=Chris |date=December 11, 2020 |title=Taylor Swift Has Her Second Great Album of 2020 With 'Evermore': Album Review |url=https://variety.com/2020/music/reviews/taylor-swift-evermore-album-review-1234851525/ |access-date=August 23, 2022 |website=Variety}}</ref> ''[[Pitchfork (website)|Pitchfork]]''{{'s}} Sam Sodomsky noted her as a \"versatile, expressive vocalist\".<ref name=\":52\">{{cite web |last=Sodomsky |first=Sam |date=December 15, 2020 |title=Taylor Swift: evermore |url=https://pitchfork.com/reviews/albums/taylor-swift-evermore/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201215214943/https://pitchfork.com/reviews/albums/taylor-swift-evermore/ |archive-date=December 15, 2020 |access-date=December 14, 2020 |website=[[Pitchfork 2021 re-recorded albums, critics began to praise the mature, deeper and \"fuller\" tone of her voice.<ref>{{Cite news |last=McCormick |first=Neil |date=April 9, 2021 |title=Taylor Swift copies her 2022 |website=The A.V. ''Midnights'' received acclaim for her nuanced vocals.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Kelly |first=Fred |date=October 21, 2022 |title=Taylor Swift's Midnights: what the critics are saying |magazine=[[The Week]] |url=https://www.theweek.co.uk/arts-life/culture/music/958268/taylor-swift-midnights-album-review |access-date=October 23, 2022}}</ref>\n\n=== Songwriting ===\n[[File:Phoenix-Musical Intrument Museum-Taylo Swift Les Pual guitar.jpg|upright|thumb|right|alt=A photograph of Swift's decorated red Les Paul guitar and cordless microphone|Swift's [[Gibson Les Paul|Les Paul]] guitar and microphone in the [[Musical Instrument Museum (Phoenix)|Musical Instrument Museum of Phoenix]]]]\n\nSwift has been referred to as one of the greatest songwriters of all time and the best of her generation by several publications.<ref>{{cite news|date=August 22, 2019|title=Taylor Swift's songwriting: how the star's music has changed, for better or worse|url=https://www.cbc.ca/amp/1.5246984|access-date=November 10, 2021|website=[[CBC Music]]}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last=Emily|first=Lee|date=November 5, 2021|title=Here Are Taylor Swift's Best Bridges On 'Red' Ranked|url=https://www.iheart.com/content/2021-11-05-here-are-taylor-swifts-best-bridges-on-red-ranked|access-date=November 10, 2021|agency=iHeartRadio}}</ref><ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Eggertsen |first=Chris |date=September 20, 2022|title=Taylor Swift's Iconic Songwriting Credits Amplified By Spotify With Dedicated Page |url=https://www.billboard.com/pro/taylor-swift-spotify-songwriter-page-launch/ |access-date=September 20, 2022|magazine=Billboard }}</ref> She told ''[[The New Yorker]]'' in 2011 that she identifies as a songwriter first: \"I write songs, and my voice is just a way to get those lyrics across.\"<ref name=\"widdicombe1\" /> Swift's personal experiences were a common inspiration for her early songs, which helped her navigate life.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/SB10001424052702304510704575562401576663866|title=Taylor Swift's Solo Act|last=Farley|first=Christopher John|date=October 22, 2010|newspaper=[[The Wall Street Journal]]|access-date=May 24, 2012|url-status=live|url-access=subscription|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150201211555/http://www.wsj.com/articles/SB10001424052702304510704575562401576663866|archive-date=February 1, 2015}}</ref><ref name=\"telltale\">{{Cite magazine|last1=Jo Sales|first1=Nancy|last2=Diehl|first2=Jessica|date=April 2013|title=Taylor Swift's Telltale Heart|magazine=[[Vanity Fair (magazine)|Vanity Fair]]|url=http://www.vanityfair.com/hollywood/2013/04/taylor-swift-cover-story|url-status=live|access-date=February 4, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170130205206/http://www.vanityfair.com/hollywood/2013/04/taylor-swift-cover-story|archive-date=January 30, 2017}}</ref> Her \"diaristic\" technique began with identifying an emotion, followed by a corresponding melody.<ref name=\"ZaneLowe\">{{cite web|url=https://www.nme.com/news/music/taylor-swift-diaristic-songwriting-style-unsustainable-future-folklore-evermore-2837843|title=Taylor Swift says her diaristic songwriting style was 'unsustainable' for her future|work=[[NME]]|first=Rhian|last=Daly|date=December 13, 2020|access-date=February 17, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130614085411/https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/474541/taylor-swifts-red-the-billboard-cover-story|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/474541/taylor-swifts-red-the-billboard-cover-story|title=Taylor Swift's ''Red'': The Billboard Cover Story|first=Phil|last=Gallo|date=October 22, 2012|archive-date=June 14, 2013|magazine=Billboard}}</ref> On her first three studio albums, love, heartbreak, and insecurities, from an adolescent perspective, were dominant themes.<ref name=\"nytimes1\">{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2010/10/24/arts/music/24swift.html?pagewanted=all|title=Taylor Swift Is Angry, Darn It|last=Caramanica|first=Jon|date=October 20, 2010|newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=July 2, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120911131428/http://www.nytimes.com/2010/10/24/arts/music/24swift.html?pagewanted=all|archive-date=September 11, 2012}}</ref><ref name=\":16\">{{Cite news|last=Kelly|first=James|url=http://www.accessatlanta.com/news/entertainment/music/taylor-swift-writing-her-own-songs-and-rules/nQy5n/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140908123045/http://www.accessatlanta.com/news/entertainment/music/taylor-swift-writing-her-own-songs-and-rules/nQy5n/|archive-date=September 8, 2014|title=Taylor Swift writing her own songs and rules|work=[[The Atlanta Journal-Constitution]]|date=August 26, 2009|access-date=July 30, 2012}}</ref> She delved into the tumult of toxic relationships on ''Red'',<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/pop/8030142/taylor-swift-red-best-album/|title=Why Taylor Swift's ''Red'' Is Her Best Album|date=November 8, 2017|magazine=Billboard|access-date=December 27, 2020 |first=Sam|last=Lansky}}</ref> and embraced nostalgia and post-romance positivity on ''1989''.<ref name=\"NPR Music\"/> ''Reputation'' was inspired by the downsides of Swift's fame,<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-features/taylor-swift-moments-that-couldnt-fit-in-our-cover-story-890700/|title=9 Taylor and ''Lover'' detailed her realization of the \"full spectrum of love\".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://onairwithryan.iheart.com/featured/ryan-seacrest/content/2019-08-27-taylor-swift-talks-newfound-freedom-lover-tour-plans-and-so-much-more/|title=Taylor Swift Talks Newfound 'Freedom,' to heartfelt disclosures\".<ref name=\"Powers\">{{cite web|url=https://www.npr.org/sections/therecord/2014/10/30/360129727/the-many-new-voices-of-taylor-swift|title=The Many New Voices of Taylor |url=https://www.grammy.com/news/artists-standing-up-for-women-taylor-swift-lizzo-harry-styles-brandi-carlile-pink-madonna-alicia-keys-ariana-grande-list |website=The Recording Academy}}</ref><ref name=\"Zach Johnson\">{{Cite magazine|url=http://www.vanityfair.com/culture/2013/03/taylor-swift-fights-back-tina-fey-amy-poehler|title=Cover Preview: Taylor Swift Fights Back About Her Love Life, the Hyannis Port House\u2014and Has Words for Tina Fey and Amy Poehler|magazine=[[Vanity Fair (magazine)|Vanity Fair]]|date=March 5, 2013|access-date=August 3, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160808192844/http://www.vanityfair.com/culture/2013/03/taylor-swift-fights-back-tina-fey-amy-poehler|archive-date=August 8, 2016}}</ref> Aside from clues in album [[liner notes]], Swift avoided talking about the subjects of her songs.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2012/11/18/magazine/the-many-insecurities-of-taylor-swift.html|title=The Many Insecurities of Taylor Swift|last=Dominus|first=Susan|date=November 16, 2012|work=[[The New York Times]]|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160617050939/http://www.nytimes.com/2012/11/18/magazine/the-many-insecurities-of-taylor-swift.html|archive-date=June 17, 2016}}</ref>\n\nOn her 2020 albums ''Folklore'' and ''Evermore'', Swift was inspired by [[escapism]] and [[romanticism]] to explore fictional narratives.<ref name=\"musicians on musicians\" /> Without referencing her personal life, she imposed emotions onto imagined characters and story arcs, which liberated her from tabloid attention and suggested new paths for her artistry.<ref name=\"ZaneLowe\" /> Swift explained that she welcomed the new songwriting direction after she stopped worrying about commercial success.<ref name=\"musicians on musicians\">{{cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-features/paul-mccartney-taylor-swift-musicians-on-musicians-1089058/|title=Musicians on Musicians: Paul McCartney and Taylor Swift|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|first=Patrick|last=Doyle|date=November 13, 2020|access-date=February 7, 2021}}</ref> According to ''[[Spin (magazine)|Spin]]'', she explored complex emotions with \"precision and devastation\" on ''Evermore''.<ref>{{cite web|last=Olivier|first=Bobby|date=December 11, 2020|title=Taylor Swift's 'Evermore' Is an Undeniable Folk-Pop Masterpiece|url=https://www.spin.com/2020/12/taylor-swift-evermore-album-review/|access-date=February 1, 2021|work=[[Spin (magazine)|Spin]]}}</ref> ''Consequence'' stated her 2020 albums provided a chance to convince skeptics of Swift had \"songwriting power\", noting her transformation from \"teenage wunderkind to a confident and careful adult\".<ref name=\":21\" />\n\nSwift categorizes her songwriting into three types: \"[[quill]] lyrics\", referring to songs rooted in antiquated poeticism; \"[[fountain pen]] lyrics\", based on modern and vivid storylines; and \"glitter gel pen lyrics\", which are lively and frivolous.<ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Shutler |first=Ali |date=October 9, 2022 |title=Taylor Swift organises her lyrics into three 'dorky' pen-themed categories |url=https://www.nme.com/news/music/taylor-swift-organises-her-lyrics-into-three-dorky-pen-themed-categories-3325355 |access-date=October 18, 2022 |magazine=NME}}</ref> Critics note the fifth track of every Swift album as the most \"emotionally vulnerable\" song of the album.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Browne |first=Erin |date=October 21, 2022 |title=All of Taylor Swift's Famously Devastating Track 5's, Ranked |url=https://www.vulture.com/article/taylor-swift-track-5-songs-ranked.html |access-date=October 27, 2022 |website=Vulture}}</ref> Swift's [[Bridge (music)|bridges]] are often underscored as one of the best aspects of her songs,<ref>{{cite web|last=Murphy|first=Sam|date=November 10, 2021|title=How 'Red' Became The Most Pivotal Record In Taylor Swift's Career|url=https://junkee.com/taylor-swift-red-importance/314415|access-date=November 10, 2021|website=[[Junkee]]}}</ref><ref name=\":21\" /> earning her the title \"Queen of Bridges\" from ''Time''.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Bruner|first=Raisa|date=May 24, 2021|title=How Olivia Rodrigo Become America's Biggest New Pop Star|url=https://time.com/6050587/olivia-rodrigo-sour/|access-date=November 10, 2021|magazine=[[Time (magazine)|Time]]}}</ref> Awarding her with the Songwriter Icon Award in 2021, the [[National Music Publishers' Association]] remarked that \"no one is more influential when it comes to writing music today\" than Swift.<ref>{{cite web|date=May 24, 2021|title=NMPA to Honor Taylor Swift with Songwriter Icon Award Among Other 2021 Annual Meeting Honorees|url=https://www.nmpa.org/nmpa-to-honor-taylor-swift-with-songwriter-icon-award-among-other-2021-annual-meeting-honorees/|access-date=May 24, 2021|website=[[National Music Publishers' Association]]}}</ref> ''[[The Week]]'' deemed her the foremost female songwriter of modern times,<ref>{{cite web|last=Linker|first=Damon|date=November 26, 2021|title=Taylor Swift, Phoebe Bridgers, and Rihanna: How women took over songwriting|url=https://theweek.com/feature/1007434/how-women-took-over-the-top-ranks-of-the-songwriting-pantheon|access-date=November 28, 2021|website=The Week}}</ref> and the [[Nashville Songwriters Association International]] named her Songwriter-Artist of the Decade in 2022.<ref name=\":31\" /> [[Carole King]] considers Swift her \"professional grand daughter\" and thanked Swift for \"carrying the torch forward.\"<ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Graff |first=Gary |date=October 31, 2021|title=Taylor Swift Helps Induct Carole King, Sings \"Will You Love Me Tomorrow\" at Rock Hall Ceremony |url=https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/music-news/taylor-swift-helps-induct-carole-king-rock-hall-ceremony-1235039810/ |access-date=September 20, 2022|magazine=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]}}</ref> Swift has also published two original poems: \"Why She Disappeared\" and \"If You're Anything Like Me\".<ref>{{cite magazine|last=Greco|first=Patti|date=November 13, 2017|title=A Harvard Professor Critiques Taylor Swift's New Poems|url=https://www.cosmopolitan.com/entertainment/celebs/a13528212/taylor-swift-poetry-harvard-professor-review/|access-date=December 21, 2021|magazine=Cosmopolitan}}</ref>\n\n=== Video and film ===\n{{Main|Taylor Swift videography}}\n\nSwift emphasizes visuals as a key creative component of her music making process.<ref name=\":13\">{{Cite news |last=Ordo\u00f1a |first=Michael |date=September 9, 2022|title=Taylor Swift wants an Oscar. So she took 'All Too Well' to TIFF |url=https://www.latimes.com/entertainment-arts/music/story/2022-09-09/taylor-swift-tiff-oscar-all-too-well-toronto-2022 |access-date=September 10, 2022|newspaper=[[Los Angeles Times]] }}</ref> She has collaborated with different directors to produce her music videos, and over time she has become more involved with writing and directing. She developed the concept and [[Film treatment|treatment]] for \"Mean\"<ref>{{cite web|author=CMT.com Staff|date=May 4, 2011|title=Taylor Swift's \"Mean\" Video Debuts Friday|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1663245/taylor-swifts-mean-video-debuts-friday/|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190619161133/http://www.cmt.com/news/1663245/taylor-swifts-mean-video-debuts-friday/|archive-date=June 19, 2019|access-date=June 19, 2019|publisher=[[CMT (U.S. TV channel)|CMT]]}}</ref> and co-directed the music video for \"Mine\" with [[Roman White]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://webcache.googleusercontent.com/search?q=cache%3A71z8LAzW7OkJ%3Awww.mtv.com%2Fnews%2F2296264%2Fvideo-taylor-swift-mine-2%2F+&cd=1&hl=en&ct=clnk&gl=us&client=safari|title=Video Premiere: Taylor Swift, 'Mine'|last=Anitai|first=Tamar|date=August 27, 2010|publisher=[[MTV News]]|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190429190835/http://webcache.googleusercontent.com/search?q=cache%3A71z8LAzW7OkJ%3Awww.mtv.com%2Fnews%2F2296264%2Fvideo-taylor-swift-mine-2%2F+&cd=1&hl=en&ct=clnk&gl=us&client=safari|archive-date=April 29, 2019|url-status=dead|access-date=June 19, 2019}}</ref> In an interview, White said that Swift \"was keenly involved in writing the treatment, casting and wardrobe. And she stayed for both the 15-hour shooting days, even when she wasn't in the scenes.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1663418/offstage-taylor-swift-isnt-mean-at-all-director-says/|title=OFFSTAGE: Taylor Swift Isn't \"Mean\" at All, Director Says|last=Bonaguro|first=Alison|date=May 6, 2011|publisher=[[CMT (U.S. TV channel)|CMT News]]|access-date=June 20, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190619161135/http://www.cmt.com/news/1663418/offstage-taylor-swift-isnt-mean-at-all-director-says/|archive-date=June 19, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\nFrom 2014 to 2018, Swift collaborated with director [[Joseph Kahn (director)|Joseph Kahn]] on eight music videos\u2014four each from her albums ''1989'' and ''Reputation''. Kahn has praised Swift's involvement in the craft.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.etonline.com/exclusive-taylor-swifts-director-joseph-kahn-how-her-image-invokes-double-standard-shes-genius|title=Exclusive: Taylor Swift's Director Joseph Kahn on How Her Image 19, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> She worked with [[American Express]] for the \"Blank Space\" music video (which Kahn directed), and served as an executive producer for the interactive app ''AMEX Unstaged: Taylor Swift Experience'', for which she won a [[Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Interactive Program]] in 2015.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/taylor-swift-wins-emmy-interactive-821735|title=Taylor Swift and Jimmy Fallon Among Early Emmy Winners|last=O'Connell|first=Michael|date=October 9, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> Swift produced the music video for \"Bad Blood\" and won a [[Grammy Award for Best Music Video]] in 2016.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.thefashionspot.com/buzz-news/latest-news/590025-taylor-swifts-bad-blood-music-video/|title=Peep Taylor Swift's Star-Studded Cast for Her 'Bad Blood' Music Video|last=Forbes|first=Jihan|website=The Fashion Spot|date=May 14, 2015|access-date=May 13, 2020}}</ref>\n\nHer production house, Taylor Swift Productions, Inc., is credited with producing all of her News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-53857694|access-date=November 9, 2020}}</ref>\n\n===Politics and activism===\nSwift refrained from discussing politics early in her career, fearing it might influence people.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://entertainment.time.com/2012/10/19/taylor-swift-on-going-pop-ignoring-the-gossip-and-the-best-worst-nickname-shes-ever-had/?iid=ent-main-lede|title=Taylor Swift on Going Pop, Ignoring the Gossip and the Best (Worst) Nickname She's Ever Had|first=Dan|last=Macsai|date=October 19, 2012|magazine=[[Time (magazine)|Time]] |access-date=July 1, 2022}}</ref> Critics took issue with her previously apolitical stance despite her wealth and celebrity.<ref name=\"Levine\">{{cite web|last=Levine|first=Nick|date=August 21, 2019 |title=Taylor Swift's ''Lover'': The struggle to maintain superstardom|url=https://www.bbc.com/culture/article/20190820-taylor-swift-and-the-struggle-to-maintain-pop-superstardom|access-date=October 29, 2021|website=[[BBC]]}}</ref><ref name=\"Hawgood\">{{cite news|url=http://www.nytimes.com/2010/11/07/fashion/07ANTHEM.html|last=Hawgood|first=Alex|date=November 5, 2010|title=For Gays, New Songs of Survival|website=[[The New York Times]]|url-access=limited|access-date=July 1, 2022}}</ref> Swift publicly voiced her political opinion for the first time in the 2018 United States elections, when she endorsed [[Democratic Party (United States)|Democratic]] candidates in her home state, Tennessee.<ref name=\"Snapes\">{{Cite news|last=Snapes|first=Laura|date=August 24, 2019|title=Taylor Swift: 'I was literally about to break'|newspaper=The Guardian |url=http://www.theguardian.com/music/2019/aug/24/taylor-swift-pop-music-hunger-games-gladiators|access-date=December 20, 2021}}</ref> In 2019, Swift told ''The Guardian'' that when she started her country music career, she was advised against discussing politics by her label executives because of the consequences of the [[Dixie Chicks controversy]], but finally decided to speak up after she became disillusioned with contemporary American politics and moved out of Big Machine.<ref name=\"Snapes\"/>\n\nShe identifies as a [[pro-choice]]<ref name=\"GuardianInterview2019\">{{cite news|last=Snapes|first=Laura|date=August 24, 2019|title=Taylor Swift: 'Pop music can feel like it's The Hunger Games, and like we're gladiators' |newspaper=The Guardian |url=https://www.theguardian.com/music/2019/aug/24/taylor-swift-pop-music-hunger-games-gladiators?|url-status=live|access-date=August 24, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190824114530/https://www.theguardian.com/music/2019/aug/24/taylor-swift-pop-music-hunger-games-gladiators|archive-date=August 24, 2019}}</ref> [[feminist]], and is one of the founding signatories of the [[Time's Up (organization)|Time's Up]] movement against sexual harassment.<ref>{{cite news|date=October 21, 2019|title=The Original 300+ Time's Up Signatories|url=https://timesupnow.org/times-up-the-300-original-signatories/|access-date=May 20, 2020|agency=Time's Up}}</ref> She criticized the [[Supreme Court of the United States|US Supreme Court]]'s [[Dobbs v. Jackson Women's Health Organization|decision]] to overturn ''[[Roe v. Wade]]'' (1973) and end federal [[Abortion in the United States|abortion rights]] in 2022.<ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Mier |first=Tom\u00e1s |date=June 24, 2022|title=Taylor Swift Says She's 'Absolutely Terrified' After Roe v. Wade Decision |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/taylor-swift-terrified-roe-v-wade-1373876/ |access-date=June 24, 2022|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]}}</ref> Swift advocates for [[LGBT rights]],<ref>{{cite news|date=June 4, 2018|title=Taylor Swift sends 'love' and 'respect' to LGBT fans|agency=[[BBC News]]|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/newsbeat-44352519|url-status=live|access-date=December 15, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181114063244/https://www.bbc.com/news/newsbeat-44352519|archive-date=November 14, 2018}}</ref> and has called for the passing of the [[Equality Act (United States)|Equality Act]], which prohibits discrimination based on sex, sexual orientation, and gender identity.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Kreps|first=Daniel|date=June 1, 2019|title=Taylor Swift video for the single \"Mean\" to note her as a musician having a positive impact on the [[LGBT community|LGBTQ+ community]].<ref name=\"Hawgood\"/> Swift performed during [[Stonewall 50 \u2013 |access-date=December 28, 2021|magazine=Vogue Australia}}</ref>\n\n== Impact ==\nAs one of the leading music artists of the 21st century, Swift has influenced the [[music industry]] in many aspects.<ref name=\":11\" /><ref name=\":14\" /> Business journalist [[Greg Jericho]] describes her as a \"cultural vitality\".<ref>{{Cite web |last=Jericho |first=Greg |date=October 28, 2022 |title=Taylor Swift's incredible success in graphs \u2013 who can blame me for being a Swiftie as a 50-year-old man? |website=The Guardian ''Billboard'' noted only few artists have had Swift's chart success, critical acclaim and fan support, enabling her to have a wide-reaching impact.<ref>{{Cite magazine |date=March 23, 2022 |title=Taylor Swift's 40 Biggest Hot 100 Hits |url=https://www.billboard.com/lists/top-taylor-swift-songs-top-100-hits/ |magazine=Billboard |access-date=April 12, 2022}}</ref>\n\nSwift helped shape the modern country music scene.<ref name=\"guardian country\">{{cite web |url=https://www.theguardian.com/music/2014/mar/13/country-music-taylor-swift-nashville-radio-2 |title=Detwanging country music: how Nashville took the UK|first=Colin|last=Crummy|work=The Guardian |date=March 13, 2014|access-date=September 23, 2021}}</ref> Rosen described Swift as the first country act whose fame has reached the world beyond the U.S.<ref name=\"Rosen\" /> Her chart success extends to Asia and the UK, where country music was not previously popular.<ref name=\"guardian country\" /><ref name=\"Rosen\" /> She is one of the first country acts to use the internet as a marketing tool, promoting her work through [[MySpace]].<ref name=\":29\" /><ref name=\"EW1\" /> Following her rise to fame, country labels became interested in signing young singers who write their own music.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/6386008/how-billboard-woman-of-the-year-taylor-swift-changed-country-music|title=4 Ways Billboard Woman of the Year Taylor Swift Changed Country Music |last=Tannembaum|first=Rob |date=September 12, 2014|magazine=Billboard|access-date=December 31, 2019}}</ref> With her autobiographical songs about romance and heartbreak, Swift introduced the country genre to a younger generation who can relate.<ref name=\":11\">{{cite magazine|last=Roland|first=Tom|date=July 7, 2016|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/7430895/taylor-swift-music-career-ten-years-impact-country|access-date=July 7, 2016|title=Love Story: The Impact of Taylor Swift's First 14, 2016}}</ref><ref name=\"Rosen\">{{cite web|url=https://www.vulture.com/2013/11/taylor-swift-reigning-queen-of-pop.html|title=Why Taylor Swift Is the Reigning Queen of Pop |first=Jody|last=Rosen|author-link=Jody Rosen|work=[[New York (magazine)|New York]]|date=November 17, 2013|access-date=November 9, 2020|url-access=limited}}</ref> Critics have since noted her musical 78&nbsp;billion streams.<ref name=\":12\">{{cite web|date=May 9, 2021|title=Taylor Swift to receive BRITs Global Icon award|url=https://www.officialcharts.com/chart-news/taylor-swift-to-receive-global-icon-award-at-the-2021-brit-awards__33098/|access-date=May 10, 2021|website=[[Official Charts Company]]}}</ref><ref 2021|website=[[BRIT Awards]]}}</ref> She has the most number-one albums in the United Kingdom and Ireland for a female artist this millennium,<ref>{{cite web|date=July 31, 2020|title=Taylor Swift's Charts}}</ref> and earned the highest income for an artist on Chinese digital music platforms\u2014{{Currency|159,000,000|RMB}}.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Wang|first=Dennis|date=April 16, 2021|title=Taylor female act on Spotify,<ref name=\":26\">{{Cite web |last=Young |first=Alex |date=October 31, 2022 |title=Taylor Swift broke 73 records with release of new album Midnights |url=https://consequence.net/2022/10/taylor-swift-midnights-records/ |access-date=October 31, 2022 |website=Consequence}}</ref> and the only artist to have received more than 200 million streams in one day (228&nbsp;million streams on October 21, 2022).<ref>{{Cite web |last= |last2= |date=October 22, 2022 |title=Taylor Swift Breaks Two Records With 'Midnights', Becoming the Most-Streamed Artist on Spotify |url=https://newsroom.spotify.com/2022-10-22/taylor-swift-breaks-two-records-with-midnights-becoming-the-most-streamed-artist-on-spotify/ |access-date=October 23, 2022 |website=Spotify}}</ref> [[Billboard Global 200#Most total entries|The most entries and the most simultaneous entries]] for an artist on the [[Billboard Global 200|''Billboard'' Global 200]], with 94 and 31 songs, respectively, are among her feats.<ref>{{Cite tweet |user=billboardcharts|number=1483944852786192388|title=Most entries on the #Global200 chart in a single week}}</ref><ref>{{Cite |url=https://www.billboard.com/pro/taylor-swifts-midnights-biggest-global-streaming-week-2022/ |url-access=subscription |access-date=November 2, 2022}}</ref> Her [[Reputation Stadium Tour]] (2018) is the highest-grossing North American tour ever,<ref name=\"reputationtour\"/> and she was the world's [[List of highest-grossing live music artists#2010s|highest-grossing female touring act of the 2010s]].<ref>{{cite web|last=Aswad|first=Jem |date=November 22, 2019 |title=U2 Tops Rolling Stones, Ed Sheeran as Highest-Grossing Touring Artist of the Decade |url=https://variety.com/2019/biz/news/u2-tops-rolling-stones-ed-sheeran-as-highest-grossing-touring-artist-of-the-decade-1203413348/ |access-date=June 29, 2020|website=Variety}}</ref> Beginning with ''Fearless'', all of her studio albums sold over a million units globally in their opening weeks.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Willman |first=Chris |date=December 21, 2020 |title=Taylor Swift's 'Evermore' Sells a Million Worldwide in First Week |website=Variety |url=https://variety.com/2020/music/news/taylor-swift-evermore-sells-million-first-week-1234867490/ |access-date=December 21, 2020 2021}}</ref>\n\nIn the US, Swift has sold over 37.3&nbsp;million albums as of 2019,<ref name=\":25\" /> when ''Billboard'' placed her eighth on its Greatest of All Time Artists Chart.<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/charts/greatest-of-all-time-artists|title=Greatest of All Time Artists|magazine=Billboard|access-date=November 15, topped the ''Billboard'' Hot 100. She is the longest-reigning act of [[Billboard Artist 100|''Billboard'' Artist 100]] (52 weeks),<ref name=\":31\" /> the soloist with the most cumulative weeks (56) atop the ''Billboard'' 200,<ref name=\":26\" /> the woman with the most Hot 100 entries (188),<ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Zellner |first=Xander |date=October 31, 2022 |title=Taylor Swift Charts All 20 Songs From 'Midnights' on top-ten songs (40),<ref name=\"BBH1002\">{{Cite magazine |last=Trust |first=Gary |date=October 31, 2022 |title=Taylor Swift Makes History as First Artist With Entire Top 10 on Billboard Hot 100, Led by 'Anti-Hero' at No. 1 |url=https://www.billboard.com/music/chart-beat/taylor-swift-all-hot-100-top-10-anti-hero-1235163664/ |access-date=October 31, 2022 |magazine=Billboard}}</ref> and weeks atop the [[Top Country Albums]] (98),<ref>{{cite web |last=Berkowitz |first=Brittany |title=Shania Twain praises Taylor Swift for breaking one of her chart records the most [[Digital Songs]] number-ones (23)<ref>{{Cite magazine|date=February 23, 2021|title=Taylor Swift's 'Love Story (Taylor's Version)' Debuts at No. 1 on Hot Country Songs Chart: 'I'm So Grateful number-one ''Billboard'' 200 debuts (11).<ref name=\":20\"/> Swift is the second highest-certified female digital singles artist (and third overall) in the U.S., with 134&nbsp;million total units certified by the [[Recording Industry Association of America]] (RIAA),<ref>{{cite news|title=RIAA \u2013 Top Artists (Digital Singles)|website=[[Recording Industry Association of
